On 9/30/05, Joe Steeve <joe_steeve@gmx.net> wrote:
> Now., these innovations may not be obvious to a business person who
> does not know the details of OS technology. A business person., or a
> end user merely terms `innovation` as what he can see. However, it is
> not so. All technical innovations need not be pleasing or acceptable to
> a business person., and vice versa. Now., that is the reason why many
> people on this thread where particular on the angle in which you were
> approaching the topic, based on your domain/expertise.

Somehow, usage of the term 'business person' seems to preclude
knowledge of technology. I have been in the chemical processing
industry (as a service engr), in the manufacturing industry (as an
owner) and in the s/w industry (as an employee) for the last 5 yrs. I
have developed applications in C, Java, Perl and PHP. I design arch
for enterprise applications now and even now write code in java
occassionally. I lead a team of 10 hotshot programmers, advice mgmt on
technology issues and take tech related decisions for my employer. So,
I use many angles to look at a problem in contrast to the narrow
programmers perspective that seems to cloud many in this list.

If any of you thought it was a rant by a naive 'business person' pls
revisit the thread. And pls tell me if this background info has helped
you see new meaning in it!!

On Sat, 2005-10-01 at 11:34, Mano wrote:
> If any of you thought it was a rant by a naive 'business person' pls
> revisit the thread. And pls tell me if this background info has helped
> you see new meaning in it!!

You got me wrong. We dont say, it is a rant. What we say is., that the
perspective matters depending on the domain of expertise. As., I said. A
person well versed in OS technology would be able to identify the
innovations that have happened in the various Free Software OSes
(gnu/linux, gnu/hurd, freebsd, netbsd, *). But., the same person wont be
able to appreciate the innovations in the Python language or its
interpreter. Computing journals such as IEEE, USENIX, etc.. carry a
number of research conclusions/proposals based on Free Software and open
technologies. Many of them are path breaking innovations, however a
python programmer., or a perl programmer need not necessarily understand
the implication of such innovations. Same goes to a business person.
That is not a degrading comment on the perl/python programmer or the
business person. If you want to read between the lines., I'm sorry.

On 10/1/05, Joe Steeve <joe_steeve@gmx.net> wrote:
> business person. If you want to read between the lines., I'm sorry.

Nothing personal, Joe :-) There was nothing in your post to irk me.
Forgive my outburst.

But your mail gives me one more chance to clarify what I meant by
'earth shaking' innovation: it is one that cuts accross domains and
makes people go 'wow'.

When a Unix system was installed in our campus in the mid 80s (yes,
late, but it was still the rule of licence raj then) and we were told
by resident eggheads that we dont have to wait for days to get results
for the programs on punched cards we submitted to the CS and that we
can work on the terminals ourselves we did go 'wow'. Then again when I
saw a mac in a printers studio it was 'wow... why didnt the unix or
the dos guys think of it!'. I was not a CS dept guy. But it still
amazed me.

Years later was humbled when I got an internet connection (missed
witnessing the browser revolution though). But soon got disenchanted
by the pathetic search results. Until google happened. Now, these are
the innovations am talking about. Not restricted to geeks but the
whole society.

Loadable modules or virtualization of filesystems in the linux kernel
are great innovations no doubt. But of restricted appeal and only for
people in the kernel field. Locale shaking, yes, but not 'earth
shaking'.

What irks me is the branding of differing points of view as 'against
the faith' and flaming/trolling all such posts to oblivion. A list
member sent me a pvt mail raising some very relevant issues. When I
asked him why he would'nt post this to the list he says he has tried
in the past but got flamed into submission. Now he is clear he wont
post anything in the list! Dont you think this is a sorry state of
affairs for the lugc community? In any organization shutting out
dissent is the first sign that all is not hunky dory as one would like
to beleive.

Again, this is not aimed at you, Joe. It is for the whole lugc
community to think about.

This really is my last post in this thread :-) Will search lugc's soul
more in other threads.

--
All those who believe in psychokinesis, raise my hand.

ok...u may not reply to this, but you could think this over...i was
too young to witness the events you are talking about, but i could
guess that for people who were deeply involved in hardware or systems,
the arrival of terminals could have as well been the next logical
step, having followed that area closely and knowing deeply about it.
on the other hand, when I first encountered XMPP(Jabber), a protocol
from the free software community, as a person interested in design in
computer science, my response was the same emphatic 'wow!'...what a
beautiful and elegant application of an extensible data format to a
network protocol....now, it would be foolish of me to expect that
every1, for that matter, every1 in the cs community, would have
perceived the innovation similarly...it is just that breakthroughs can
never be universally appreciated...ok, some are distinctly more
important than others...but imho, universality can never will, and
never should be a goal we should strive at...

it moves on...

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Oct  1 04:27:41 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Oct  1 16:57:52 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Mailing list guidelines
Message-ID: <20051001112741.83074.qmail@web50206.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

This is a monthly reminder of the mailing list
guidelines. Please don't reply to this e-mail. If you
would like to update it, do it at:

http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/List_Guidelines

1. Do not troll in the mailing list

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_troll

2. Do not post off-topic [OT] messages in this mailing
list. Use ilugc-non-tech@googlegroups.com instead.

3. Do not top-post

Example of a top-post:

  I think you should be swapping the arguments around
in the 
  function, instead of the way you are doing it.
  On Friday, the 13th, you said:
  > I am using the function xyz(), giving arguments
arg1 and arg2, 
  > but it does not work. Anyone know why?

Always use bottom-posting.

  On Friday, the 13th, you said:
  > I am using the function xyz(), giving arguments
arg1 and arg2, 
  > but it does not work. Anyone know why?
  I think you should be swapping the arguments around
in the 
  function, instead of the way you are doing it.

Check this link:

http://www.caliburn.nl/topposting.html

4. Do not over-quote

Example of an over-quote:

  >>> On Friday you said
  >>> blah blah blah
  >> On Saturday you said
  >> foo foo foo
  > On Sunday you said
  > foobar

5. Do not post HTML messages

6. Do not recycle messages

7. Do not send attachments

8. Do not attach obnoxious, nonsensical legal
disclaimers

  If your company uses disclaimers, don't use your
company ID for the mailing list.

9. Do not reply to a digest. (If you are in digest
mode and want to reply to a post use our blog
interface
(http://blog.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc))

10. Search for answers for your questions/problems in
google.com or any other search engine before posting
your query to the mailing list.

If any of the above are not clear to you, please read
the detailed list rules:

  http://www.catb.org/~esr/faqs/smart-questions.html

If you violate any of these rules, your message will
be deleted, so if you are posting and don't see your
messages appearing on this list, check whether you
have followed the rules while posting.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Sat Oct  1 19:37:22 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Sat Oct  1 19:35:08 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (HOST)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510011932410.22177-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Prof Andrew S. Tanenbaum (AST) Author of many OS and Network Books
and Creator of Minix & Amoeba OS. URL: http://www.cs.vu.nl/~ast/

One Day One Command 
===================

host -- DNS Look-up Utility

Summary:

host is a simple utility for performing DNS (Domain Name Service)  
lookups.  It is normally used to convert names to IP addresses and
vice versa.

Examples:

$ host google.com -- Show the IP Address of Google.com.

$ host -v google.com -- Show detailed output.

$ host -a google.com -- Show more details.

$ host 127.0.0.1 -- Do reverse lookup and Show the host name.

$ host -l mydomain.com -- List all hosts available in MyDomain.

Read: man host

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Sun Oct  2 03:41:25 2005
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)
Date: Sun Oct  2 08:11:33 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Tata Indicom walky phone lg-350T usb connection in linux
Message-ID: <20051002024125.54476.qmail@web8603.mail.in.yahoo.com>

Today I could successfully connect internet using Tataindicom walky 
model lg-350T with usb port -dialup on debian sarge without any
difficulty.
Details are
1.debian detected the device and loaded cdc_acm module.
2.wvdialconf automatically detected and created config file
3.only init2 strings needs change

run wvdial <connectionname> connected to internet.

The wvdial.conf is as follows
[Dialer Defaults]
Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
Baud = 460800
Init1 = ATZ
#Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0 This is autodetected 
#but not working changed as follows. Thanks to sudarshan
Init2=AT+CRM=1
ISDN = 0
Modem Type = USB Modem
Stupid Mode=on
Dial Command=ATDT
Phone = #777
Username =internet
Password = internet

Thanks to sudarshan for providing his wvdial configuration.

Raman.P

> Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (SYNC)
> To: GNU/Linux User Group - Madurai
> 	<glug-madurai-discuss@lists.sourceforge.net>, 	GNU/Linux User Group of

> 	<Pine.LNX.4.44.0509271902480.12414-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
> Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
>
> Eric S. Raymond (ESR), Well known Hacker in FOSS & Unix World, Author
> of "The Cathedral and the Bazaar" & "Art of Unix Programming", and
> maintainer of the "Jargon File". URL: http://www.catb.org/~esr/
>
> One Day One Command
> ===================
>
> sync -- Flush File System Buffers.
>
> Summary:
>
> The Linux Kernel keeps data in memory to avoid doing (relatively slow)
> disk reads and writes.  This improves performance, but if the computer
> crashes, data in memory may be lost or the file system corrupted as a
> result.
>
> `sync' used to Synchronize data on disk with memory. 'sync' writes any
> data buffered in memory out to disk.
>
> Examples:
>
> $ sync -- Write buffered data to disk.
>
> Read: man sync
>
> HTH :)
> --
> Bharathi S
> ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/
>

> From: Binand Sethumadhavan <binand@gmail.com>
> Subject: Re: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (SYNC)
> To: ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in
> Message-ID: <d2a92d610509271325574dadc8@mail.gmail.com>
> Content-Type: text/plain; charset=ISO-8859-1
>
> On 27/09/05, Senthil Kumaran <stylesen@gmail.com> wrote:
> > I have a doubt.. why there is a need for sync.. why the data is not
> > witten to the memory as soon as it is reffered to.. is it important to
> > have this delay...
>
> Bharti's summary explains it:
>
> "The Linux Kernel keeps data in memory to avoid doing (relatively slow)
> disk reads and writes.  This improves performance, but if the computer
> crashes, data in memory may be lost or the file system corrupted as a
> result."
>
> The kernel automatically flushes these in-core buffers as and when
> they become full; the sync(8) command (and the sync(2) system call) is
> for forcing this flush operation.
>
> Binand

> > Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (SYNC)
> > To: GNU/Linux User Group - Madurai
> > 	<glug-madurai-discuss@lists.sourceforge.net>, 	GNU/Linux User Group of
> > 	TCE <glugot@tce.edu>, <linux4all@gmail.com>,	Indian Linux Users Group
> > 	- Chennai <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>,	NRC FOSS-TTP
> > 	<nrcfoss-ttp@lists.deeproot.co.in>
> > Message-ID:
> > 	<Pine.LNX.4.44.0509271902480.12414-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
> > Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
> >
> > Eric S. Raymond (ESR), Well known Hacker in FOSS & Unix World, Author
> > of "The Cathedral and the Bazaar" & "Art of Unix Programming", and
> > maintainer of the "Jargon File". URL: http://www.catb.org/~esr/
> >
> > One Day One Command
> > ===================
> >
> > sync -- Flush File System Buffers.
> >
> > Summary:
> >
> > The Linux Kernel keeps data in memory to avoid doing (relatively slow)
> > disk reads and writes.  This improves performance, but if the computer
> > crashes, data in memory may be lost or the file system corrupted as a
> > result.
> >
> > `sync' used to Synchronize data on disk with memory. 'sync' writes any
> > data buffered in memory out to disk.
> >
> > Examples:
> >
> > $ sync -- Write buffered data to disk.
> >
> > Read: man sync
> >
> > HTH :)
> > --
> > Bharathi S
> > ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

> > > witten to the memory as soon as it is reffered to.. is it important to
> > > have this delay...
> >
> > Bharti's summary explains it:
> >
> > "The Linux Kernel keeps data in memory to avoid doing (relatively slow)
> > disk reads and writes.  This improves performance, but if the computer
> > crashes, data in memory may be lost or the file system corrupted as a
> > result."
> >
> > The kernel automatically flushes these in-core buffers as and when
> > they become full; the sync(8) command (and the sync(2) system call) is
> > for forcing this flush operation.

Lately, there seems to be several self proclaimed
rulers are dictating their views as the 'acceptable
behaviour' to participate intelligent discussions.

So I ask the 'Authority' to say

Who is the current List Administrator ?

When did the list's 'Guidelines' turn into 'Rules' ?

Way back when there were only guidlelines and
participants used their own sanity except on
occassions tempers flew due to sun-flares,
bad music etc., Eventually, still participants
behaved with tolereance and cool and the list 
moved on.

Who are these present day Rulers? are they attempting
to become one ?  They give me the creeps
with their threats 'the posts will be deleted',
No more 'OT' etc., 

Last, I did enjoy very much the intellectual
discussion went on recently in reponse to
Mr. Mano.  So, I would like to see more of it
with [OT] or whatever tags  smart people 
decide to put in front of it.  Again,
participants can simply ignore it if they
don't like the author or the tags. I request
'facism' be not allowed to creep into this list.

I for one appreciate posts from Biand, SivaSankar,
Chandrasekar and several others.  

If my comments are unacceptable. please let
me know and I will gladly oblige by unsubscribing.

Rudy Colbert

Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> writes:
> Loadable modules or virtualization of filesystems in the linux
> kernel are great innovations no doubt. But of restricted appeal
> and only for people in the kernel field. Locale shaking, yes,
> but not 'earth shaking'.

Ok., I get what you mean. Well., that is quite true. However, that
is not the case only with Free Software., it is as such a case
with the entire Software Industry. After a point in Science and
Technology, the innovations get confined to a very narrow area.,
which surely does not appear path-breaking to common man. 

But., targetting the lack of innovation due to saturation, towards
the Free Software community is something that is not
acceptable. In fact, in today's scenario most of the advanced
research get implemented in Free Software rather than their closed
source counterparts. The only cases when superior technology is
not implemented is when the concerned technology is patented or
has some crap of that sort attached to it. 

The argument that `lack of incentive kills innovation` is not
true. Take UNIX as an example. When its developers started out.,
Bell was not really supporting the project because they had
already blown out a lot of money in the MULTICS project. The
developers still created UNIX in their free time because of their
passion towards programming/developing/*. So., today's lack of
``earth-shaking`` innovations may be due to the saturation in this
field.

> What irks me is the branding of differing points of view as
> 'against the faith' and flaming/trolling all such posts to
> oblivion. A list member sent me a pvt mail raising some very
> relevant issues. When I asked him why he would'nt post this to
> the list he says he has tried in the past but got flamed into
> submission. Now he is clear he wont post anything in the list!
> Dont you think this is a sorry state of affairs for the lugc
> community? In any organization shutting out dissent is the first
> sign that all is not hunky dory as one would like to beleive.

Hmm., well. I really cannot comment on this. However, this list
has had experience of mindless flame-baits. Non constructive
arguments going in circles. But many times., a flame-war has
happened because someone just decided to forget/ignore some
facts. ``Flame wars and Arrogance`` is not the picture that the
``Free Software Community`` wants to show to the world.

On 10/2/05, Joe Steeve <joe_steeve@gmx.net> wrote:
> Ramanraj K <ramanraj.k@gmail.com> writes:
> > 1997, but I would like to know if India does have a backbone
> > atleast now.
>
> Hmm., I think the STPI is working on something like this. They are
> creating some sort of nodes around the country interlinking ISPs
> so that for a traffic between two Chennai ISPs need not travel all
> across the world.


India does have a backbone. Way back in 1998/1999 (or earlier) I
remember going through an article in Computers Today. It mentioned
something around 400 mbps or 300Mbps (+/- 150Mbps) backbone in our
country and that 50% was not utilized!

And I remember seeing the pipes passing through ernakulam, and madras
when I did traceroutes here and there sometime in/around 2000.

The backbones those days were gateway'd to FLAG (which I think was
purchased by Reliance last year, for millions) for international
connectivity.

And yes, there is a new set of links/hubs around the country. And
there are some plans for IRC servers (are they already on the network?
DALnet?) on some of these Internet Exchanges (IXs) too... this means a
*lot* of bandwidth.

ps: My views could be outdated/incorrect. I am no more into network
stuff and it has been a really long time since I checked on these
things.


--
Arvind Kalyan
http://www.devforge.net/~arv

----- Fwd Message -----
Hi, 

My name is Vikram Vijayaraghavan. The pt of this email is: I am back
in India (from the US) to setup the Indian operations (in Chennai) of
the startup I work for, Efficient Frontier (www.efrontier.com) and
thus looking to hire some smart engineers.

The core of our work is all Python based and the UI framework uses
struts/jsp. Please take a few minutes to read the job posting (sorry
for any crossposting) :

---
First about the startup: The startup is in the search-marketing space
wherein it applies optimization theory to deliver maximum performance
to online advertising campaigns. What this means, in a very naive way,
is the adverts you see in Google/Yahoo etc websites are all
dynamically bid on in a real-time auction to get top positions with
constraints of total budget, seasonality etc . The whole system can
hence be modelled as a very involved optimization/math problem and we
have some of the best minds in that field working on this. The
engineering problem of creating a feedback loop by getting data from
search engines and the customers and collating/processing that data
and using that to execute new bids realtime is enormous and this is
just one dimension of the problem.

To give you an idea of scale, total online ad revenue is around
$11billion a year in the US alone. We were first-movers in this area
and today we are the largest data-gatherers from Google and Yahoo.
Most of the top e-commerce websites are clients and we ourselves
manage more than 150million USD per year revenue. This space is
"redhot" as the marketing folks like to put it.
----

We are looking for three kinds of engineers. Obviously, more
experienced the better, but I am open to hiring people with less
experience if they are really smart. The positions are:

a) Systems Engineers with a good software engineering background,
   Some DB experience a must. Good C/C++ skills, python experience a
   huge plus. Must be a good "systems" person overall

b) QA/Test engineers: People who are familiar with standard testing
   concepts and who can write a whole test framework from scratch.

c) UI engineers: People with experience in the struts/jsp framework.
   People with a decent UI background who are more than anything very
   enthusiastic about UI work.
 
Some of the obvious advantages are : top-notch payscale - get paid in
dollars; will match competitor pay and more, stock options - startup
is 2 years old so you can get a very good payout with your options,
visa/greencard processing while working in Chennai, excellent/very
informal work-culture.

Do take a look to see if you are interested. At the very least, please
forward it to any lists and suggest people who might be interested
(and get referral fees). I would be glad to discuss this in more
detail with anyone. Either email me at vvikram@stanford.edu /
vvikram@gmail.com or call me at 91-44-24996092.

Regards,
Vikram

Subject: [Ilugc] About the List and the wannabe Rulers

On Sun, 2 Oct 2005, Rudy Colbert wrote:

> So I ask the 'Authority' to say Who is the current List
> Administrator ?

In our Oct month meeting only, We have to finalize the next person the
List Admin Post.

> When did the list's 'Guidelines' turn into 'Rules' ?

It is only Guideline. I made few changes in monthly mailing list
reminder and send to Shakthi. Here attaching the Guideline with some 
extra additions. I hope, it is in accpectable form ? :)

=====

1. Use Proper Subject Line.

2. Do not Troll in the mailing list

Link: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_troll

3. Do not post off-topic [OT] messages in this mailing list. Use
ilugc-non-tech@googlegroups.com instead.

Off-Topic == Topic, which is not related to FOSS and Linux.

4. Do not Top-Post

Link: http://www.caliburn.nl/topposting.html

 Example of a top-post:

 A: Because it messes up the order in which
    people normally read text.
 Q: Why is top-posting such a bad thing?
 A: Top-posting.
 Q: What is the most annoying thing in e-mail?

 Always use bottom-posting.

 Q: What is your name ?
 A: My name is ILUGC.

5. Do not Over-Quote

 Example of an over-quote:

 >>> On Friday you said
 >>>  blah blah blah
 >> On Saturday you said
 >>  foo foo foo
 > On Sunday you said
 >  foobar

6. Do not post HTML messages

7. Do not recycle messages

8. Do not send attachments

9. Do not attach obnoxious, nonsensical big legal disclaimers. If your
company uses disclaimers, try to avoid using your company ID for the
mailing list.

9. Do not reply to a digest. (If you are in digest mode and want to
reply to a post use ILUGC Gmane blog interface.

Link: http://blog.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc

10. Search for answers for your questions/problems in google.com or
any other search engine before posting your query to the mailing list.

If any of the above are not clear to you, Please follow the link:

Link: http://www.catb.org/~esr/faqs/smart-questions.html

We should try to follow the above guidelines to maintain better
readability, Proper Archices, Efficient Bandwidth usage, etc...

=====

> They give me the creeps with their threats 'the posts will be
> deleted', No more 'OT' etc.,

No. 

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

   Dear Swamy,
   I am glad to inform you that we have successfully implemented the
   installation, training and handholding of 'Min Aluvalagam', paper-less
   office solution in the Head Office of Sports Development Authority of
   Tamil Nadu, India, in a short span of 30 days, using OPEN SOURCE tools
   such as Java, JBoss with PGSQL as backend, all running on Linux.

   The implementation of the tool has transformed the work culture of the
   organization and all employees right from the Tapal Section Assistant who
   is an 8th class pass to the Member Secretary are willingly using the tool.
   All incoming letters are scanned and digitized and from then on moves
   electronically and attached to e-Files which get instant approval and
   outward tapal is sent. This has dramatically improved the service level
   and cut down the average process time by 50%. A copy of the Certificate
   issued by Mr. P.W.C. Davidar, IAS, Member Secretary, Sports Development
   Authority of Tamil Nadu, is attached..

   This is a unique e-Governance initiative. The tool complies fully with the
   Tottenham system of office administration, followed in the Secretariat,
   Governmentt departments and undertakings. We can integrate any language
   and Digital Signature into the tool.

   We have implemented the tool in Electronics Corporation of Tamil Nadu Ltd.
   (ELCOT), a Govt. of Tamil Nadu Undertaking, for the last almost 2 years,
   based on which, they have entered into a marketing agreement with us.

   We have implemented a customized paper-less communication solution for
   Industrial Guidance Bureau, Govt. of Pondicherry, connecting 19
   departments / municipalities / panchayats on a simple dial-up, for
   granting time bound and transparent clearance.
   We had implemented the solution in the Office of the Spl. Commissioner of
   Treasuries and Accounts, Chennai for five months from Jan to May 2005.

   We look forward to the pleasure of hearing from you and the opportunity of
   servicing any requirement thro' your good offices, as it is the right
   time, considering the Right to Information Act. Our tool can be adopted as
   an e-Governance tool by any Government organiation.

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Mon Oct  3 12:10:57 2005
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy)
Date: Mon Oct  3 12:08:39 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] CPU affinity in Linux
Message-ID: <4340D279.90305@tandbintl.com>

    "Simply stated, CPU affinity is the tendency for a process to run on 
a given CPU as long as possible without being moved to some other 
processor. The Linux kernel process scheduler inherently enforces what 
is commonly referred to as soft CPU affinity, which means that processes 
generally do not frequently migrate between processors. This state is 
desirable because processes that seldom migrate often incur less overhead.
    "The 2.6 Linux kernel also contains a mechanism that allows 
developers to programmatically enforce hard CPU affinity. This means 
your applications can explicitly specify which processor (or set of 
processors) a given process may run on..."

For more details, click here: 
http://www-128.ibm.com/developerworks/linux/library/l-affinity.html

          collisions:0 txqueuelen:0

eth0     Link encap:  HWaddr 00:0C:E5:52:6F:B3

          inet6 addr: fe80::20c:e5ff:fe52:6fb3/64 Scope:Link

          RX bytes:256942 (250.9 KiB)  TX bytes:39980 (39.0 KiB)
          Interrupt:11 Memory:14400000-14401fff 

lo is a needed loopback 
If there is anything more, perhaps eth0, shut it done with
# ifconfig eth0 down
Check that it is gone with:
# ifconfig
Then start the dialout.

From Jacques.Goldberg at cern.ch  Sun Oct  2 10:33:53 2005
From: Jacques.Goldberg at cern.ch (Jacques Goldberg)
Date: Mon Oct  3 15:19:17 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Authentication problem in India, with Agere soft Modem
In-Reply-To: <100120051753.27772.433ECD210009E05000006C7C22064244130B019B9C909D0E03@comcast.net>
References: <100120051753.27772.433ECD210009E05000006C7C22064244130B019B9C909D0E03@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <433F8D61.6010102@cern.ch>

Sir,

As Marv points out, the modem is working fine and has nothing to do with 
your problem.


I fail to understand exactly what happens because in your earlier report 
(visible at the end below and named case #1 in my reply) you write that 
you are connected but cannot get a reply from the DNS which has been 
assigned, while in the second report just below you show that you cannot 
LOGIN.

There are three steps in the procedure before you can make any usage of 
the connection, even pinging an address:

1-you dial and the modem on the other side answers. This is clearly working.

2-the program   pppd   is started on both sides.

3-Either the ISP computer in general (computer, not modem) or your 
computer sometimes, start an authentification procedure,

which in case #2 clearly fails.

If any of the step above fails, it makes no sense to try to use the 
connection, it CANNOT and WILL NOT work.

To understand what went wrong in phase 3 of case #2, it is necessary to:

-edit /etc/ppp/options

-insert in it a line  with the word   debug

-save and exit the editor

-try again to connect

-right after the procedure ends which in your case makes the message 
"The PPP daemon has died. (exit code = 19)",

find close to the end of the file /var/log/messages a line "pppd 
started" or equivalent.

-copy that part of the file (not to send the very large complete file) 
from "ppp started" to "The PPP daemon has died"

for analysis, for which you can choose between:

 -doing it yourself using   
http://www.cisco.com/warp/public/471/debug_ppp_negotiation.html .

 -send us that part of the file (again, PLEASE do not send the whole 
file). If this is your choice, please also send your file

/etc/ppp/options .


One only among a large number of possibilities could be that your files 
/etc/ppp/pap-secrets and chap-secrets is not empty

(i.e. nothing in it or no line NOT starting with a # sign): if this is 
your case, add a leading # where there is none and try again.


Jacques



Are these two ways to express the same problem, or did problem #2 occur 
after you connected as in case #1?


Was the failure observed in #2 already there but ignored in case #1?

On 03/10/05, Mohan SK <mohanbarathi@gmail.com> wrote:
> *Hi all,*
> *Is there any way to change password using script?*
> *MohanBarathi.*

Well, it depends on what you want to do.

If you are root, you can write your own wrapper with the passwd
--stdin version of the passwd command.

If you are a normal user, you should look at an expect based script.

If you are a web developer, DO NOT create your website users as Unix users.

If you are a systems administrator, you ought to look at cfengine.

If you are a programmer, it is easy to write code that does whatever
you want - using the functions in pwd.h and shadow.h. Slightly more
difficult is to have hooks to PAM and use all its features.

Binand

Try it as a root,

# echo "MyPassword" | passwd --stdin UserName

On Mon, 03 Oct 2005 15:51:15 +0530, Mohan SK <mohanbarathi@gmail.com>  
wrote:

> *Is there any way to change password using script?*

If you wish to change password of other users as root,
you can try the 'chpasswd' command. A simple example
of how you would change the passwd of a user called
tux to w31c0m3 would be as follows:
    echo tux:w31c0m3 | /usr/sbin/chpasswd

Try 'man chpasswd' for a more formal documentation.

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

From sudharsh at gmail.com  Mon Oct  3 17:46:19 2005
From: sudharsh at gmail.com (Sudharshan S)
Date: Mon Oct  3 17:46:09 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] re: how to install from tar files
Message-ID: <43412113.4010209@gmail.com>

hi,
First of all note that tar balls contain the source of the package, so 
you must compile them first. normally most of the tarballs contain a 
configure script which tries to guess your pcs configuration and then 
creates a file called makefile which in turn contains all the 
instructions for compilation, after compilation u can install the 
packages by issuing 'make install', u may also want to specify certain 
flags say for example where you would like to install the software. lets 
go in detail
open the terminal,
cd to the place where u have downloaded the tarball
issue 'tar -xvzf <name of the package>' this cmmand extracts the files
cd into the root of extracted directory
issue './configure', usually the software installs itself in /usr/local 
, if dont have root access you may also specify custom locations by 
'--prefix=/location/of/ur/choice'
after some messages and if there are no dependency errors or similar, 
issue 'make' command.
the software will compile, after this issue 'make install', if u get 
errors while installing try again as root, otherwise the dir onto which 
u r installing does not have write access,
thats it,
also remember to always read README, INSTALL files present in the 
tarball as they may contain some special info regarding installation and 
usage, if you hav any doubts jus contact me n i'll b glad to help

regards
Sudharshan S

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Mon Oct  3 18:39:10 2005

	<2bd916e50510030523j3070201fxc8184397ba8ef28d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <op.sx2mtkhrv8spko@xaero.intranet.vetrije.com>

On Mon, 03 Oct 2005 17:53:16 +0530, Mohan SK <mohanbarathi@gmail.com>  
wrote:

>  I want a normal user to change their password using the script.

Then the following expect script should suffice (though it doesn't
handle all possible cases of automating passwd command):

-------- cut here ----------
#!/usr/bin/expect -f
spawn passwd
set oldpass [lindex $argv 0]
set newpass [lindex $argv 1]

expect "password:"
send "$oldpass\r"

expect "password:"
send "$newpass\r"

expect "password:"
send "$newpass\r"

expect eof

------- cut till here ------

Assuming that you saved this script into a file named 'chpasswd.expect',
and made this file executable, try running this script the following
way:
   ./chpasswd.expect oldpassword newpassword

If you want to automate interactive commands using perl/python/ruby
or similar languages, there would be better ways to achieve them
without depending on the 'expect' command. You might want to
read up on controlling pseudo-TTYs if that were the case.

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

rave... i have already told u this.... add these options to ur fstab!!!

/dev/hdb1       /mnt/Debian     reiserfs        exec,rw,user,auto

Hi,

> Anybody has installed xine Or gxine, mplayer on
> sarge.
> apt-get install is not  working

You can compile mplayer from source code:

1. Download essential-codecs-version package first and
extract it. 

2. Download MPlayer-version package and extract it. 

Both can be obtained from here:

http://www.mplayerhq.hu/homepage/design7/dload.html

3.Enter into MPlayer sources directory and do:

   $  ./configure
--with-codecsdir=/path/to/essential-codecs 
   $  make

As root do:

   #  make install

HTH,

SK

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Oct  4 19:58:33 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Oct  4 19:55:48 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (HALT)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510041958020.27840-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Prof. Douglas Comer, author of the Network & OS Books and Creator 
of Xinu OS. URL: http://www.cs.purdue.edu/people/comer

One Day One Command 
===================

halt -- Stop the System.

Summary:

Halt notes that the system is being brought down in the /var/log/wtmp,
file and then either tells the kernel to halt, reboot or poweroff the
system. Halt invoke shutdown, if the system is not in runlevel 0 or 6.

Examples:

# halt -- Halt the system.

# halt -f -- Force the Halt.

# halt -i -- Shutdown the Network interface before Halt.

# halt -p -- When Halting the system, Do a Power off.

# poweroff -- Same as above.

Read: man halt

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

>   I want to convert my Mails which is in mbox format to PST format
> compatible with Outlook/Outlook Express.

setup imap in linux machine and place your mbox file for a user and download 
the mails to outlook. In this way you can convert either way. Or just 
configuring pop3 and doing the above steps will convert mbox to Outlook 
format.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Oct  6 18:51:42 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Oct  6 18:48:18 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (SCRIPT) (fwd)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510061851200.6372-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Dennis Ritchie, Core developer of Unix OS and Creator of C Language.
URL: http://www.cs.bell-labs.com/who/dmr/index.html

One Day One Command 
===================

script -- Record the user's activities on a terminal.

Summary:

Script makes a typescript/record of everything printed on your
terminal. It is useful for anyone, who need a hard copy record of an
interactive session as proof, and the typescript text file can be
printed.

Press Ctrl+D/exit/logout to Stop the Script Program.

Examples:

$ script -- Start the recording in a file (Default File Name 
            is typescript).

$ script MyFile -- Record the output in MyFile.

$ script -a -- Record the output in Appending Mode.

$ cat typescript -- Show the recorded content.

Read: man script

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Oct  6 07:20:24 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Oct  6 19:50:39 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] installing Ubuntu in IBM Thinkpad T52

Message-ID: <20051006142024.42031.qmail@web50201.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- kamal r <kamalsubramanian@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Hi,
>   I have an IBM Thinkpad T52 which has a single

Awesome machines to run GNU/Linux.

> partition with Win XP as OS. 

Did you boot into windoze?

When the thinkpads arrive from the factory, the hard
disk is formatted with fat32. When you boot it the
first time into windoze, the fat32 is converted to
ntfs. Huh! You will need to partition for GNU/Linux.

> I would like to install
> Ubuntu as dual boot with the orignal Win XP intact.

Most recent distros do the dual boot setups for you.
So, it shouldn't be a problem. Just make sure you
install grub/lilo to the MBR of the hard disk.

Have fun,

SK

If you only want to run servers, there are lot of
"free as in freedom" distros that you can use.

I run Debian GNU/Linux servers on HP 5500 at work.

> Can it be possible to
> update from ES3.0 to 4.0 or I have reinstall the

I believe distros have an upgrade option, when you
boot from the installation CDs, that simply update the
libraries.

Its always good to keep /home or any other data on a
separate partition so you don't have to worry about
upgrades affecting your data.

> guidence what precautions i have to take.

Backup your data, just in case, before proceeding.

References: <20051006101018.10492.qmail@web30405.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <8816fcf80510061037v18e01d84vdd248e5f21bb4ec6@mail.gmail.com>

On 10/6/05, kamal r <kamalsubramanian@yahoo.com> wrote:
>
> Hi,
> I have an IBM Thinkpad T52 which has a single
> partition with Win XP as OS. I would like to install
> Ubuntu as dual boot with the orignal Win XP intact.
> Could anybody provide me with pointers to resources
> on the web.


Hi Kamal,

I own a T52. I had formatted my HD and installed Ubuntu on it. The best
thing you can do is better format the whole harddisk and install Windows on
a preformatted patition using the serial key provided at back of your
thinkpad (you can use your friend's windows CD and it is perfectly legal).
Then install Ubuntu over any of the free partition. Please note that you
have to download all drivers/software that came with thinkpad's windows
installtion from the IBM site - http://www.lenovo.com/think/in/en/

The other methods including resizing, recovering to IBM rescue disks didn't
work for me as expected.

--
Sridhar Ratna - http://srid.multiply.com/

Check out this link (about the SC400, predecessor to the SC420):

http://www.poweredgeforums.com/showthread.php?t=2236&page=1&pp=30

Dell is still using the Nichicons in later systems, but you may have got an

hangs and exceptions, check out the capacitors immediately.

From manokaran at gmail.com  Fri Oct  7 11:37:56 2005
From: manokaran at gmail.com (Mano)
Date: Fri Oct  7 11:38:14 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] nessus goes closed source
Message-ID: <7bf1bec50510062307w781ca661o6d429ff5047a6f48@mail.gmail.com>

An intriguing post in slashdot about the venerable nessus going closed source:

http://news.com.com/Nessus+security+tool+closes+its+source/2100-7344_3-5890093.html?tag=nefd.hed

The motivation seems to be related to some points I raised in the 'To
provoke thought..' thread: Competitors somehow bypassing the GPL and
still benefitting from the improvements made by the original author.
The original author ends up spawning competition (and also feeding
them) and ends up losing! If Renaud Deraison is to still keep nessus
ver 3 open source, what will be his motivation to improve it and more
importantly, what will be his motivation to invent a new product?

Of course, Fyodor is against it and says he is happy with GPLed Nmap.
But different strokes for diff folks. Maybe Renaud Deraison covets a
Ferrari but Fyodor does not! It doesnt mean Deraison is evil! Or is
he?

regds,
mano

All those who believe in psychokinesis, raise my hand.

The maximum file size in a FAT32 partition is 4GB. that's why i guess
k3b crashes at 85% which happens to be near the 4GB border.

NTFS is capable of handling larger files and same is the case with ext2 (IIRC).

Try ripping the DVD to some other partition with a different filesystem.

On 10/7/05, Zulfi <zulfilee@midascomm.com> wrote:
> On Fri, 2005-10-07 at 14:52 +0530, Chakkaradeep C.C. wrote:
> > Hi all,
> > i received this message in a forward mail ... try this..
> > An Indian discovered that nobody can't create a folder anywhere named as
> > "con"
> >

The way in which DOS used to handle the console was using the name con
for console. So going by the same architecture Windows also doesn't
allow you to create with names viz.
con - for console, com1 - for serial port 1, lpt1 etc.

To send a file to serial port (COM1) one can issue the copy command
with target as com1.

--
Jayakumar K K

	<992fa2e60510070327t11e6ed70x288718fa88b41a84@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610510070341q374d0ef4s@mail.gmail.com>

On 07/10/05, Jayakumar K K <kkjayakumar@gmail.com> wrote:
> As far as I know there are nothing. The problem with DOS or Windows
> for that matter is that, it doesn't deal with devices with Major or
> Minor numbers as linux handles.

The Linux way is based upon "everything is a file" paradigm. For
example, on Linux you can do things like:

mknod /home/binand/mydevices/myserialport c 4 64

and use /home/binand/mydevices/myserialport in any software that uses
a serial port - your dialling software or your remote console
software, for example. There is no loss of functionality, nothing.
There is nothing sacrosanct about /dev/ttyS0. /dev is just a
convenient location for collecting all "special" files which are not
plain files or directories or sockets or pipes.

Binand

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Oct  7 19:21:40 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Oct  7 19:18:07 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (DU)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510071921100.3764-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Brian W Kernighan, Core developer of the Unix OS, Creator of the C
Language and author of many book. 
URL: http://www.cs.bell-labs.com/who/bwk/index.html

One Day One Command 
===================

du -- Print the file's disk space usage.

Summary:

du summarize disk usage of each file/Dir, recursively for directories
and print the info in different format. Normally the size is printed
in units of 1024 bytes.

Examples:

$ du -- Show the disk usage of present and it's all sub Dirs
        (recursively).

$ du -a -- Show the files size also along the Dir.

$ du -h -- Show sizes in the Human readable format (1K, 2M).

$ du -S -- Don't include the Sub Dirs size.

$ du -s -- Show total size of the current Dir. No detailed listing.

$ du -X MyExcPat -- Exclude all files, which is matching with the 
                    patterns(*txt, *awk, *.c) in the 'MyExcPat' file.

$ du --exclude="*.pdf" -- Exclude all PDF files.

$ du --max-depth=2 -- Travel only 2 level depth below the current Dir.

$ du -b MyFile -- Show the 'MyFile' size in Bytes.

$ du -h MyDir -- Show the 'MyDir' size in Human readable form.

Read: man du

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Fri Oct  7 07:43:44 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Fri Oct  7 20:13:58 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Doubt in Linux dir naming convention
In-Reply-To: <20051007142039.92470.qmail@web34402.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20051007144345.52042.qmail@web50209.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Anandh G <anandhg02@yahoo.com> wrote:
> I have a doubt in the Linux system dir (like etc,
> var) naming convention.

The Linux kernel does not have any system directories.
The GNU/Linux system as such has it.

> What does "etc" exactly
> mean. 

etcetra? etc has all system configuration files.

var means "variable", for having varying file sizes.

> How does this folders got this name.

There is no hard-and-fast rule. Its just a name that
is easier to remember and that is common for all to
use. If you build a distro from scratch (LFS for
example), you can name the directories in whichever
way you want.

opersys guide:
http://www.opersys.com/dox/opersys-quickref-1.0.5.pdf

When creating the directories for your ${PRJROOT}, you
can name it whichever way you want.

Some useful links:

http://wiki.arslinux.com/Linux_Directory_Hierarchy

http://www.redhat.com/docs/manuals/linux/RHL-9-Manual/ref-guide/s1-filesystem-fhs.html

http://gd.tuwien.ac.at/linuxcommand.org/lts0040.html

SK

--

On 10/7/05, Sridhar Ratna <sridharinfinity@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> Shouldn't this even depend on the filesystem implementation?

 Let me start with an example. The file names CON, LPT1, PRN, etc., can be
created on a FAT16 file system, by directly manipulating the FAT tables
(write your own program. Ref. Peter Norton's System programming book -
forgot the exact name though). You will have to use an old version of DOS
(DOS 6.22 or earlier) for trying out this.
 But there are certain restrictions as imposed by the operating system. I am
not very sure, if we can create a file called CON from Linux on a fat32 file
system, as I am using a friend's PC. I was able to create files with names
containing #255 in it, under DOS. But I had problems accessing it through
Windows. Thus I would summarize it like, your file system doesn't restrict
you to create certain file names. It is just the program that you use to
make the entry into the tables, makes the restrictions. So if we try to use
another program (or write our own) to make changes to the entries, we can
virtually create any kind of file names.

Rgds,
Natarajan.

<mail@atulchitnis.net> writes on the
http://groups.yahoo.com/group/foss-in-announce/ list:

          This is it, the last day of speaker and talks
          registration for FOSS.IN/2005.

By midnight tonight (October 8th), we will be closing
registration for talks for the technical and community
sessions of the event. Speakers who have registered but not
submitted any talks will be removed from the speaker database
tonight.

          So if you are planning to submit any talks - you
          have till midnight tonight (GMT+0530!)

FOSS.IN seems to be generating massive amounts of enthusiasm
in the Linux community, and *especially* in the BSD community
(who have proposed several talks and workshops), the Gentoo
community, the Debian community, etc.

The FOSS community rulez!

I will send in another mail giving you some top level stats
about talks and speakers once we close registrations tonight.

          Once registrations close, we will spend a couple of
          days sorting things out, checking which talks need
          work on, and will release the first shortlist
          (minus work-in-progress talks and "star" talks) on
          schedule in the evening of the 12th of October. 
          (See the schedule at http://foss.in/2005/cfp/).

Once clashes and WIP talks are sorted out, we will release a
second list with these added. "Star" speakers will be
announced as soon as the remaining major sponsor
confirmations come in.

Call for participation for business sessions and student
talks will go out early next week. Stay tuned. Atul

WANTED, CODERS FOR AN EDUCATIONAL DEVELOPMENT-ORIENTED GAME:
Sunil Abraham sunil@mahiti.org of Bangalore sent across this
note from his friend Dev <dev@thairuralnet.org> who put
forward a specific proposal.

          Dev wrote: "I need your help to find young social
          technopreneurs (in your circle its probably Open
          source software engineers who might want to design
          a game like WFP Food Force or other software)."

Global Knowledge Partnership's Youth Social Enterprise
Initiative (YSEI) fellowships are designed to help social
entrepreneurs achieve their goals from the initial idea
through to project implementation and impact creation. 

They seek to support projects by young people who are
creating impact with innovative solutions to social problems,
especially those using information and communication
technologies (ICTs) for development. YSEI will support
fellows by providing mentorship and training programmes;
networking; and seed grants.

If you are a young social entrepreneur (age <30) from India,
Sri Lanka, Bangladesh, Philippines and Malaysia in search for
support and opportunities. Please visit
www.globalknowledge.org/ysei OR www.futureshifters.net to
learn more and submit your proposal by 31st October 2005.

Youth Social Enterprise Initiative (YSEI) is a Global
Knowledge Partnership (GKP) Youth Program supported by the
Swiss Agency for Development and Cooperation (SDC). Its
partners include MITRA, OrphanIT, TakingITGlobal,
YoungAsiaTelevision, Philippines Resources for Sustainable
Development (PRSD), Development Research Network (D.Net) with
TRN as the intiative's lead.

Sunil Abraham <sunil@mahiti.org> also happens to be manager
of the IOSN.net In addition, he's behind the Mahiti group in
Bangalore. http://www.mahiti.org 314/1, 7th Cross, Domlur
Bangalore - 560 071 Karnataka, INDIA Ph/Fax: +91 80 51150580.
Mob: (91) 9342201521 UK: (44) 02000000259

WHY GNU/LINUX NEEDS A MENTOR PROGRAM: See this interesting
essay at
http://business.newsforge.com/article.pl?sid=05/09/13/1816200&from=rss

Why Linux needs a mentor program By: Tarun Agnani: Imagine
you're a new Linux user. You ordered an Ubuntu CD weeks ago
and forgot about it. You're surprised it actually comes in
the mail. You slap the shiny disc into your PC and cross your
fingers. The installation is quite slick. You're impressed by
the splash screen and attractive desktop. Wow, you think
you're hot stuff -- a Linux user. But the euphoria fades as
you realize there's a problem with your modem. Now what do
you do? ...

FLOSS FELLOWSHIPS FROM SARAI: V Vivek <viyyer@sarai.net>
announces the Sarai/CSDS Short Term FLOSS Fellowship,
2005-2006.

          The Sarai Programme, Centre for the Study of
          Developing Societies, Delhi (www.sarai.net) invites
          applications for fellowship to projects in the area
          of Free Software, Open Source Software and Social
          Usage of Software.

Sarai invites developers, researchers and programmers
(practitioners as well as students) to propose projects in
the area of free and open source software applications
relevant to educational, social and community needs. They are
looking for original ideas, as well as proposals to localize
and adapt existing software and applications to South Asian
conditions. They are also looking for ideas around technical
manuscripts, beginners' manuals, review manuscripts etc.

Some of the focus areas are:

- Indic Computing
- Developing/Distributing/Supporting a standalone / addon
  localized  Linux distribution
- Printing support (i.e. ability to print in Indian
  Languages)
- Multimedia / Publishing Tools Research
- Developing / Enhancing Tools like GIMP, Scribus for
  publishing quality work
- Enhancing current audio/video tools available under
  Linux
- Fixing/Supporting Cinelerra, LiVES etc
- P2P
- Researching on feasibility and implementation of P2P news
  distribution network
- Researching and developing
- Collaboration Tools/Frameworks
  (Apnaopus, CreativeDot  ) 
- Developing extensions for the project newsrack
  http://floss.sarai.net/newsrack 
- Low Resource Computing
- Devising solutions for networked computing in Low Resource
  Spaces (Define the parameters of the "low resource space"
  and work on it)
- Generic
- Developing Linux drivers/software for easily available
  hardware (usually the cheapest hardware available on the
  market is not supported under Linux (scanners, webcams etc))
  [This would include writing a howto on how to get it to
  work under popular distributions (redhat, pcqlinux etc) and
  all.]
- Review papers on emerging technologies
  - Indic Computing
  - IPV6
  - Wireless Networks
- Manuscripts for beginners

For more information visit www.sarai.net. Sarai says it "is
committed to promoting the free software and open source
vision".

Conditions: Applicants should be resident in India, and
should have a bank account in any bank operating in India.
These are support grants and grantees will be free to pursue
their primary occupations, if any. Mail your project
proposal, workplan and CV to both the following addresses:
floss at sarai.net
<https://mail.sarai.net/mailman/listinfo/prc> 

Please mark your subject line 'FLOSS (Free/Libre Open Source
Software) Initiative'.  Also point out what you see as the
relevance of your work, and how you plan to share the
resultant software once finalized.

Enquires: floss at sarai.net

Note: Proposals from teams, partnerships, collectives,
faculty are welcome, so long as the grant amount is
administered by a single individual, and the funds are
deposited in a single bank account in the name of an
individual. *** Knowlege is power... share it equitably!

> Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (DU)
> To: GNU/Linux User Group - Madurai
> 	<glug-madurai-discuss@lists.sourceforge.net>, 	GNU/Linux User Group of

> Message-ID:
> 	<Pine.LNX.4.44.0510071921100.3764-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
> Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
>
> Brian W Kernighan, Core developer of the Unix OS, Creator of the C
> Language and author of many book.
> URL: http://www.cs.bell-labs.com/who/bwk/index.html
>
> One Day One Command
> ===================
>
> du -- Print the file's disk space usage.
>
> Summary:
>
> du summarize disk usage of each file/Dir, recursively for directories
> and print the info in different format. Normally the size is printed
> in units of 1024 bytes.
>
> Examples:
>
> $ du -- Show the disk usage of present and it's all sub Dirs
>         (recursively).
>
> $ du -a -- Show the files size also along the Dir.
>
> $ du -h -- Show sizes in the Human readable format (1K, 2M).
>
> $ du -S -- Don't include the Sub Dirs size.
>
> $ du -s -- Show total size of the current Dir. No detailed listing.
>
> $ du -X MyExcPat -- Exclude all files, which is matching with the
>                     patterns(*txt, *awk, *.c) in the 'MyExcPat' file.
>
> $ du --exclude="*.pdf" -- Exclude all PDF files.
>
> $ du --max-depth=2 -- Travel only 2 level depth below the current Dir.
>
> $ du -b MyFile -- Show the 'MyFile' size in Bytes.
>
> $ du -h MyDir -- Show the 'MyDir' size in Human readable form.
>
> Read: man du
>
> HTH :)
> --
> Bharathi S
> ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/
>

> Hi,
>
> --- Anandh G <anandhg02@yahoo.com> wrote:
> > I have a doubt in the Linux system dir (like etc,
> > var) naming convention.
>
> The Linux kernel does not have any system directories.
> The GNU/Linux system as such has it.
>
> > What does "etc" exactly
> > mean.
>
> etcetra? etc has all system configuration files.
>
> var means "variable", for having varying file sizes.
>
> > How does this folders got this name.
>
> There is no hard-and-fast rule. Its just a name that
> is easier to remember and that is common for all to
> use. If you build a distro from scratch (LFS for
> example), you can name the directories in whichever
> way you want.
>
> opersys guide:
> http://www.opersys.com/dox/opersys-quickref-1.0.5.pdf
>
> When creating the directories for your ${PRJROOT}, you
> can name it whichever way you want.
>
> Some useful links:
>
> http://wiki.arslinux.com/Linux_Directory_Hierarchy
>
> http://www.redhat.com/docs/manuals/linux/RHL-9-Manual/ref-guide/s1-filesystem-fhs.html
>
> http://gd.tuwien.ac.at/linuxcommand.org/lts0040.html
>
> SK

> On 10/7/05, Sridhar Ratna <sridharinfinity@gmail.com> wrote:
> >
> >
> > Shouldn't this even depend on the filesystem implementation?
>
>  Let me start with an example. The file names CON, LPT1, PRN, etc., can be
> created on a FAT16 file system, by directly manipulating the FAT tables
> (write your own program. Ref. Peter Norton's System programming book -
> forgot the exact name though). You will have to use an old version of DOS
> (DOS 6.22 or earlier) for trying out this.
>  But there are certain restrictions as imposed by the operating system. I
> am
> not very sure, if we can create a file called CON from Linux on a fat32
> file
> system, as I am using a friend's PC. I was able to create files with names
> containing #255 in it, under DOS. But I had problems accessing it through
> Windows. Thus I would summarize it like, your file system doesn't restrict
> you to create certain file names. It is just the program that you use to
> make the entry into the tables, makes the restrictions. So if we try to use
> another program (or write our own) to make changes to the entries, we can
> virtually create any kind of file names.
>
> Rgds,
> Natarajan.
>

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Oct 10 19:04:13 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Oct 10 19:01:39 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (MPSTAT)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510101903500.19981-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Dr. Bjarne Stroustrup, designer and implementor of C++ language.
URL: http://www.research.att.com/~bs/homepage.html

One Day One Command 
===================

mpstat -- Report processor(s) related statistics.

Summary:

The mpstat command writes to standard output activities for each
available processors, processor 0 being the first one. Global average
activities among all processors are also reported.

Examples:

$ mpstat -- Show statistics about all processors.

$ mpstat -P 1 -- Show the statistics info about processor 1.
                 (Note: 0 is 1st, 1 is 2nd, ...)

$ mpstat 5 -- Show the statistics for every 5 sec.

$ mpstat 5 5 -- Show 5 reports of statistics for all processors at 5
               second intervals and calculate the average at the end.

Read: man mpstat

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

Its your choice.

I would format it with a new journalling filesystem
that has better recovery, compared to what you had
with RH9.
 
> And whats the meaning of "Grub loading Stage2" ??

In short, stage1 loads stage2. Stage2 loads the boot
configuration file.

For your reference,

Grub technical info:
http://www.uruk.org/orig-grub/technical.html

GNU Grub boot loader:
http://www.linuxgazette.com/issue64/kohli.html

On 10/10/05, Prashanth <prashmohan@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> out of topic but.. would anyone know of any DNS servers that can be used
> freely? the BSNL dataone DNS server sux big time


4.2.2.1 <http://4.2.2.1>: RNS at Bolt Beranek and Newman (BBN) - now part of
Verizon.
BBN are the guys who developed the first ARPAnet IMPs
(predecessors to routers) in 1965. This RNS, however,
was commissioned only in the late 80s or 90s.

(i put 192.168.1.1 <http://192.168.1.1>
> which is the private ip of their DNS server on my resolv.conf file)


This may not work unless you've set up routing/NAT/mangling
in such a way that your non-routable packets reach that DNS server,
which IMHO won't happen easily. YMMV.

-Siva

From vishnu.vijayaraghavan at gmail.com  Tue Oct 11 08:05:28 2005
From: vishnu.vijayaraghavan at gmail.com (Vishnu Vijayaraghavan)
Date: Tue Oct 11 08:05:37 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] USB bluetooth dongle which works in Linux
In-Reply-To: <654433ee0510092306h3c3e8d9due90fed6f6db2a0d5@mail.gmail.com>
References: <654433ee0510092306h3c3e8d9due90fed6f6db2a0d5@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <809586140510101935t14a9d93cy2280a27b84ae621c@mail.gmail.com>

On 10/10/05, Shiva KM <kmshiva@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi,
>      I'm looking for a Bluetooth dongle which I can plug into the USB
> port which will work in Linux. I am running both Ubuntu 5.04(on an
> Compaq nx5000 laptop) and Slackware 10(on an nforce2 based mobo).

Any USB Bluetooth Dongle with CSR (Cambridge Silicon Radio) chipset
works fine in Linux. Bluez also supports CSR well.

>       From what I've heard from some friends, there are some dongles
> available for less than Rs.400 from ritchie street (the usual brand x,
> made in china, taiwan or something) which work in windows, though I
> havent had the opportunity to try them out in linux.

My USB Bluetooth dongle was also brought from Ritche Street (brand x,
made in china). But, it had the CSR Chipset, so my Dongle works fine
in LINUX. Make sure you bye a CSR Chipset USB Bluetooth Dongle.

 Brand doesn't matter, Chipset matters.


V.Vishnu

About CIOSA :-
=============

CIOSA, (Confederation of Indian Organisations for Service and Advocacy
is a collaborative forum for non-profit organisations,which brings
NGOs, socially motivated individuals and corporate houses on to a
common platform for mutually beneficial relationships by helping,
learning and sharing knowledge, resources and time. Non-profit
organizations remain the central focus of CIOSA. As of now there are
120 NGOs 5 corporates and 43 individuals in our network.

We continuously try to built the capacities of our NGOs, as one of our
efforts we would like to have a work-shop on FOSS for our members in
the second week of October. In this we seek your assistance in
developing content and organising the programme.

Our Members:

1. CIOSA has member groups of varied causes. NGOs working for 
   Children, Women, Old, Disabled, etc...
2. From both urban and rural.
3. 80% of them are small and medium size group.
4. Not many are computer savvy. *****
5. Have problem with English.

What we Intend to achieve:

   optimise their resource.
2. Tamil search or interfaces.

Hello Nava ladi,


1)Check wether the smbd is running if not running you cant recieve message
and start smb

/etc/init.d/smb start

2)Did you configure your smb.conf file.If not try out with this

In the file /etc/init.d/smb.conf

workgroup = workgroupname       
server string = yourcomputername    
 message command = /usr/local/bin/linpopup "%f" "%m" %s; rm %s

and now try sending the message

better try sending the message using computer name instead of ip address

(or)

3)Try with this

echo "prabu" | smbclient -M prm-co

4)for ip

echo "prabu" | smbclient -M prm-co -I 172.16.1.35



-- Cheers
Prabu.M.A

Subject: [Ilugc] Internet - BroadBand in Ubuntu !
Message-ID: <73c077240510120322n4f611388ke1679b8c4a7dcbfe@mail.gmail.com>

Hello Friends,
I installed ubuntu yesterday to solve my no-linux-on-my-machine problem ( :p ).
As my main need is internet, i asked the mailing list to help me.
Later i found the way to setup broad band connection in Ubuntu from
their Help site. Here is the Procedure so that it will be usefull for
others in future:

Configuring PPPoE for ADSL Connection in Ubuntu :
------------------------------------------------------------------

* ppp0e configuration is installed default during most Ubuntu
installations. To check whether it has been installed, type the
following @ shell/terminal
                         dpkg -l | grep -i ppp0e

* If Ubuntu has installed pppoeconf, the output willl be something like this:
              ii pppoeconf 1.1ubuntu1 configures PPPoE/ADSL connections

* If its not the above output then you have to install pppoeconf, as follows:
                 sudo apt-get install ppp0econf
* After the installation you can configure the pppoeconf. You will
need just ur username and pasword and a bit of common option's
answers. Select always on, as ti is best suggsted by Ubuntu itself.
To configure:         sudo ppp0econf

* extra tips:
# To start the connection: pon dsl-provider
( I have a doubt ?! whether we have to type it as dsl-provider or type
the name of the provider such as 'dataone' or the username
'user@dataone' ?? )
# To end the connection: poff ( I tried to end my connection, it says
cannot kill ppp0 so im not able to manually end it)
# To get the status: plog ( It too doesnt work, do we have to use
'cat' command ?? )  or ' ifconfig ppp0' ( i suggest this, it provides
u with better info)

Thank You,

yet installed FC4 :D More queries regarding it will continue ;)

10 - 15 mins of browsing using the Mozilla-Firefox browser, something
gets wrong that i am not able to open the web pages using the browser.
But, the connection is active and i am able to use GAIM. Ane idea ??

following.

too slow. I can't use array slicing here as the job done in one
iteration depends on the previous iteration. So I decided to go for
writing the code in C and wrapping it in Python. I found SWIG to be nice
and easy to use, wrote the C code. But I couldn't use Numeric arrays
that are central to my code.

Hi,

--- "T.KaruppuSwamy" <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:
> File Formats of almost all files we use day to day
> is explained here: 

Very few GNU/Linux applications make use of filename
extensions. 

There is no meaning for filename extensions in the
*nix environment. 

You can still have a foobar.tar.bz2 filename for a
.tar.gz file and extract it using:

  tar xzvf foobar.tar.bz2

> accidentally i deleted  a folder which contains
> most important info.
> we have a fc 1 server and i opened my home folder
> from a client which runs fc3. i just gave delete(not
> even shift+delete) the folder which deleted is not in
> my trash
>
> is there any way to restore the folder
> it is urgent.

You might want to look at ext2 undeletion howto. If your filesystem is ext3 
as per this FAQ 
(http://batleth.sapienti-sat.org/projects/FAQs/ext3-faq.html) you cant.

But the actual file contents will most probably exist on the device. So if 
the files are just ascii you might get some part of it by doing something 
like cat /dev/hdx|strings |grep "some unique strings".

-logu

To make it clearer for the uninitiead, if your resolv.conf look it

search xyz.com <http://xyz.com>

If you ping abc it will take below as the FQDN

abc.xyz.com <http://abc.xyz.com>

I just tried and it looks like you can have multiple search lines too. I
didn't read (the manual) though

On 12/10/05, benjamin <benjaminrtz@gmail.com> wrote:
> I just tried and it looks like you can have multiple search lines too. I
> didn't read (the manual) though

If you are on Redhat/derivatives, you wouldn't have found the man page either.

Pick up the man page from
https://bugzilla.redhat.com/bugzilla/attachment.cgi?id=115041 and save
it as /usr/share/man/man5/resolver.5 (optionally gzip it) and then do
man resolver for the documentation.

Ref: https://bugzilla.redhat.com/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=150765

Binand

From prabu.ayyappan at gmail.com  Thu Oct 13 09:15:49 2005
From: prabu.ayyappan at gmail.com (Prabu)
Date: Thu Oct 13 09:50:56 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] kpopup.
In-Reply-To: <d05619590510120731y7add1248nab18ed258e3bdbad@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d05619590510120731y7add1248nab18ed258e3bdbad@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <434DD86D.8000900@gmail.com>

nava ladi wrote:

>i am using kpopup programe.It installed well.i can send message to
>host.but my system not receive the message.but it shows tha "the
>message is  sent".Where it sent?can u pls figured  it out
>
Security problem: versions 0.9.1 - 0.9.5pre2 have a securityproblem with 
the suid-bit
On a multiuser-system it is possible that KPopup create a root shell. If 
you delete the suid-bit of KPopup, it is not possible to recieve messages.
(chmod -s /opt/kde/bin/kpopup adapt path!)

Ref:
http://www.henschelsoft.de/kpopup_en.html

-- Cheers
Prabu.M.A

2000/XP/2003 formats documented there.

> =============

saravanan mad wrote: 
,----
|  hai  to everybody,i  need help.how  to install  xine player  in linux
| fedora.iam a layman to linux
`----

Declaring yourself a layman/newbie is  no excuse to not knowing how to
install. But before that:

1. Don't Top Post.
2. Change the Subject appropriately (or better, create a new thread).

To install xine, you would first want to find out which distro you are
running. You  can then  download (or search  in your distro's  CD) the
appropriate  binary package  of xine  for your  distro and  install it
using your distro's installation utilities (ex: rpm -> redhat, apt-get
-> debian, etc.,.).

HTH

  -Suraj

From toufeeqh at gmail.com  Thu Oct 13 14:03:04 2005
From: toufeeqh at gmail.com (Toufeeq Hussain)
Date: Thu Oct 13 14:03:16 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux Distribution building
In-Reply-To: <434E0AE0.9000907@tandbintl.com>
References: <434E0AE0.9000907@tandbintl.com>
Message-ID: <c293dd340510130133w2f81fb0eo4750ed40f5358988@mail.gmail.com>

HI,

my personal opinion.

On 10/13/05, T.KaruppuSwamy <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:
>
> Dear all,
>
> I have planned to be a unofficial project guide for a Computer Science
> and Engg. students. I am thinking of going for a "Linux Distribution
> Building". I have a few queries on this:


Building a linux distro is something that a engg student does as an
hobby.There's nothing innovative in building a LFS.A case of "been there
done that".

Final year Engg students should think of new innovative/creative projects on
the Linux platform rather than re-inventing the wheel.

How about one of the projects on sourceforge.net <http://sourceforge.net> ?
Try to find a orphaned project which interests the student and implement
missing functionality to it.SF.net <http://it.SF.net> has many projects
which are either half-completed or are orphaned by their original
authors,that should provide an excellent base for a BE project.Ofcourse,it

On 10/13/05, Prashanth <prashmohan@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> in that case does this line make sense?
> search 61.1.96.69 <http://61.1.96.69> 61.1.96.71 <http://61.1.96.71>


No, you need to put in two lines:

nameserver 61.1.96.69 <http://61.1.96.69>
nameserver 61.1.96.71 <http://61.1.96.71>

These are(were?) the BSNL primary and secondary nameservers
respectively. I don't know what they're running now, but in the past
these used to get cracked and/or crash frequently. So I added the
BBN nameserver 4.2.2.1 <http://4.2.2.1> above these two, and used dnsmasq
(a lightweight replacement for bind) to perform dns caching locally.

-Siva

On 10/13/05, saravanan mad <ashwathcres2002@gmail.com> wrote:
>  hai to everybody,i need help.how to install xine player in linux
> fedora.iam a layman to linux
>
>
>  On 10/12/05, ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in <ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in>
> wrote:
> >
> > Send ilugc mailing list submissions to
> > ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in


Please don't top post. Qoute only relevant text, not the entire mail.
If you want to start a new thread don't use reply.
As for your question, fedora comes with yum. Either sudo or su - or
log into root and then do yum install
the sequence of cmd could be
$sudo yum install xine
{enter user acc. passwaord here}

--or --
If you have not configured your user account to sudoer's list then use:
$su - root
{enter root password}
#yum install xine

if either of them reutrns package not found or something similar try
adding more respositories to /etc/yum/repo.d/<repo-name.d>. Some
repositories could be fedora-extras(if u r using FC4 then its already
configured to use fedora-extra), livna, freshrpm, dags, etc.
There are lots of article on how to configure yum on fedora over the
net. try seraching the seth vidhal's pages or fedorafaq.org or
fedoranews.org or fedora-list. if you can't find in any of these then
google for it. The man pages of yum seems to be a bit outdated, anyway
could be a usefull info.

HTH

--ashwin

From sbharathi at midascomm.com  Thu Oct 13 21:03:15 2005
From: sbharathi at midascomm.com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Oct 13 20:59:41 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (GPHOTO2)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510132102410.5402-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Students, Are you looking for a Beginner level Project in Compiler?
Check it. URL: http://gcc.gnu.org/projects/beginner.html

One Day One Command 
===================

gphoto2 -- Client to access the Digital cameras.

Summary:

gphoto2 is a command-line client written using the gphoto2 cross
platform digital camera library. We can access the digital cameras,
which is connected to a GNU/Linux System thru the USB Port.

Examples:

$ gphoto2 -- Show help message.

$ gphoto2 --list-cameras -- List all supported cameras.

$ gphoto2 --list-ports -- List supported port devices.

$ gphoto2 --auto-detect -- List detected cameras.

$ gphoto2 --camera "USB PTP Class Camera" -- If camera is not auto 
                            detected the specify the generic type.

$ gphoto2 -a -- Show camera abilities.

$ gphoto2 -P -- Get all files from camera.

$ gphoto2 -p 1,4-6 -- Get only photos 1,4,5,6.

$ gphoto2 -T -- Get all thumbnails images.

$ gphoto2 --debug -- Show more detailed info. Useful to debug.

Read: man gphoto2

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Oct 13 08:43:29 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Oct 13 21:13:42 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux Distribution building
In-Reply-To: <c293dd340510130133w2f81fb0eo4750ed40f5358988@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20051013154330.1177.qmail@web50206.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

My thoughts below:

> On 10/13/05, T.KaruppuSwamy <swamytk@tandbintl.com>
> wrote:
> I am thinking of going for a
> "Linux Distribution
> Building". I have a few queries on this:

You have to show as to how different it is from the
other distros.

1. It could be built with a new package management
system.

2. It can be a minimal distro with packages that suits
a particular group of professionals. For example,
dentists or firemen?

3. It could be useful to people at a particular
instant: for example: a distro that can help people
during disasters. There were some discussions on this
in slashdot. 

4. You have to define the following:
platform/hardware, distro size, intended audience etc.

You will definitely learn a lot, but, you have to be
clear with your objectives and intended purpose of the
project.

Have fun,

SK

how? How does one access RSS feeds on Linux. Software which use RSS as

technologies, some reflections and discussion on accessibility of data
on web, which concerns RSS etc.

Greetings!

I would like your thoughts on project workflow
management software available for GNU/Linux.

Google returned this useful link:

http://linas.org/linux/pm.html

There are plenty of them, but, I need suggestions from
people who are already using one.

I would prefer one that is a stand-alone application,
but, it is fine if its web-based that can be used by
all developers in a LAN.

I want a tool  that can be used to prepare a roadmap
for a project, which in turn can be divided into
sub-tasks. Notes should be written for each sub-task,
and at the end of the project it should be possible to
provide a complete documentation/history of the
project with the above notes. 

This is to give an understanding and estimate on the
solution paths taken during project development, paths
where backtracking was done, or simply a quick
reference on the lessons learnt from the project.

MrProject has limited features, but, I would
appreciate any other recommendations.

Thanks,

On 10/13/05, Prashanth <prashmohan@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Sivasankar Chander wrote:
> >
> >
> > I added the
> > BBN nameserver 4.2.2.1 <http://4.2.2.1> <http://4.2.2.1> above these
> two, and used dnsmasq
>
> I am probably being a real pain by now ;-) but u now use "nameserver
> 127.0.0.1 <http://127.0.0.1>" as the first line of your resolv.conf to use
> the local dns cache?
>

No, not needed. The other machines on the LAN, however, have
"nameserver <non-routable-ip-address of the dnsmasq host>"
(say 192.168.0.254 <http://192.168.0.254>) and nothing else, to take
advantage of the DNS
caching for the local network only. In other words, I'm running my
own local DNS server that caches the contents of the 4.2.2.1<http://4.2.2.1>RNS
(and optionally the two BSNL nameservers or any other nameserver
for that matter), for use by all the hosts on the internal LAN.

-Siva

 On 10/13/05, Shakthi Kannan <cyborg4k@yahoo.com> wrote:
>
> Hi,
>
> My thoughts below:
>
> > On 10/13/05, T.KaruppuSwamy <swamytk@tandbintl.com>
> > wrote:
> > I am thinking of going for a
> > "Linux Distribution
> > Building". I have a few queries on this:
>
> You have to show as to how different it is from the
> other distros.
>
> 1. It could be built with a new package management
> system.
>
> 2. It can be a minimal distro with packages that suits
> a particular group of professionals. For example,
> dentists or firemen?
>
> 3. It could be useful to people at a particular
> instant: for example: a distro that can help people
> during disasters. There were some discussions on this
> in slashdot.
>
> 4. You have to define the following:
> platform/hardware, distro size, intended audience etc.
>
> You will definitely learn a lot, but, you have to be
> clear with your objectives and intended purpose of the
> project.
>
> Have fun,
>
> SK

> Please don't top post. Qoute only relevant text, not the entire mail.
> If you want to start a new thread don't use reply.
> As for your question, fedora comes with yum. Either sudo or su - or
> log into root and then do yum install
> the sequence of cmd could be
> $sudo yum install xine
> {enter user acc. passwaord here}
>
> --or --
> If you have not configured your user account to sudoer's list then use:
> $su - root
> {enter root password}
> #yum install xine
>
> if either of them reutrns package not found or something similar try
> adding more respositories to /etc/yum/repo.d/<repo-name.d>. Some
> repositories could be fedora-extras(if u r using FC4 then its already
> configured to use fedora-extra), livna, freshrpm, dags, etc.
> There are lots of article on how to configure yum on fedora over the
> net. try seraching the seth vidhal's pages or fedorafaq.org<http://fedorafaq.org>or
> fedoranews.org <http://fedoranews.org> or fedora-list. if you can't find
> in any of these then
> google for it. The man pages of yum seems to be a bit outdated, anyway
> could be a usefull info.
>
