> Message: 9
> Date: Thu, 13 Oct 2005 21:03:15 +0530 (IST)
> From: Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@midascomm.com>
> Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (GPHOTO2)
> To: GNU/Linux User Group - Madurai
> <glug-madurai-discuss@lists.sourceforge.net>, GNU/Linux User Group of
> TCE <glugot@tce.edu>, <linux4all@gmail.com>, Indian Linux Users Group
> - Chennai <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>, NRC FOSS-TTP
> <nrcfoss-ttp@lists.deeproot.co.in>
> Message-ID:
> <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510132102410.5402-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
> Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
>
> Students, Are you looking for a Beginner level Project in Compiler?
> Check it. URL: http://gcc.gnu.org/projects/beginner.html
>
> One Day One Command
> ===================
>
> gphoto2 -- Client to access the Digital cameras.
>
> Summary:
>
> gphoto2 is a command-line client written using the gphoto2 cross
> platform digital camera library. We can access the digital cameras,
> which is connected to a GNU/Linux System thru the USB Port.
>
> Examples:
>
> $ gphoto2 -- Show help message.
>
> $ gphoto2 --list-cameras -- List all supported cameras.
>
> $ gphoto2 --list-ports -- List supported port devices.
>
> $ gphoto2 --auto-detect -- List detected cameras.
>
> $ gphoto2 --camera "USB PTP Class Camera" -- If camera is not auto
> detected the specify the generic type.
>
> $ gphoto2 -a -- Show camera abilities.
>
> $ gphoto2 -P -- Get all files from camera.
>
> $ gphoto2 -p 1,4-6 -- Get only photos 1,4,5,6.
>
> $ gphoto2 -T -- Get all thumbnails images.
>
> $ gphoto2 --debug -- Show more detailed info. Useful to debug.
>
> Read: man gphoto2
>
> HTH :)
> --
> Bharathi S
> ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/
>
> WARNING: Cross Posted. Don't blindly reply.
>

From vamlists at gmx.net  Fri Oct 14 11:13:55 2005
From: vamlists at gmx.net (Vamsee Kanakala)
Date: Fri Oct 14 11:10:26 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] project workflow management software
In-Reply-To: <20051013174150.87190.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20051013174150.87190.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <434F459B.5040700@gmx.net>

Shakthi Kannan wrote:

>I want a tool  that can be used to prepare a roadmap
>for a project, which in turn can be divided into
>sub-tasks. Notes should be written for each sub-task,
>and at the end of the project it should be possible to
>provide a complete documentation/history of the
>project with the above notes. 
>  
>
What you're saying suspiciously looks like an issue tracker to me. I 
would recommend Edgewall Trac, we use it extensively at Ma Foi Systems 
Group for bug & issue tracking. It's a bit tricky to set up (but dead 
easy on Debian), written in python, runs on Apache2 and every decent 
open source project is using it or shifting to it. Here is the link:

http://projects.edgewall.com/trac

It has built-in facility for making milestones and checking your entire 
project roadmap. Added advantage is it's excellent binding with 
subversion - you can browse your checked-in code through trac, and refer 
to files/tickets through numbers very easily. Added to that, it has a 
wiki built-in! If you have any trouble setting it up, I'll be glad to 
help. Or if you want a demo, I'll give it on sunday when you come to Ma Foi.

Vamsee.

Hello Sarav,

you can use mount to see windows file in linux


$ mount  //172.16.1.35/SharedDocs /mnt
$ cd /mnt


SharedDocs is the Shared folder in windows partition
Now mnt will contains the windows file

Hi,
 If it is windows, first check what filesystem is your partition. If it is
FAT32, then it would mount automatically. If it is NTFS and ntfs not
supported, it would throw error while mounting. You have to download the
ntfs rpms for your kernel. You would have to do this if you are using Fedora
Core or RedHat distributions.
 the link where u can get ntfs rpms for fedora core and redhat is ,
http://linux-ntfs.sourceforge.net/rpm/index.html
 regards,
C.C.Chakkaradeep

On 10/14/05, sami nathan <meetsami@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> i am working on dynamic dns server, ( as we have in windows )
>
> i have dhcp and dns (linux RHEL 3) server, I tried to integrate them,
> so that my
> dhcp should update DNS,


I guess that you want a FQDN (like
<something.dyndns.org<http://something.dyndns.org>>
or similar)
to resolve to your ISP-supplied dynamic IP address, even if that
changes from time to time.

I use dyndns.org <http://dyndns.org>, and the ddclient daemon works fine for
this purpose.
YMMV - you may have to tinker with its configuration to get it working.

-Siva

Hi,
after installing suse 10, i want to put my comments....
The installation seems to be too good,
well tailored in such a way that you need to answer very few questions, 
and at the same time , you are kept informed of what all happening.. 
what packeges are installed etc... but i didnt find any custom package 
installation options as in redhat....
It didnt recognize my touchpad at installation time. .. so the 
installation took  in a semi graphic environment , not much impressive 
to see... as everything appeared in blue and red....
but once the system booted, its really wonderful...
i really wondered, is this my PC giving such cool renderings....
the rendering engine is very very impressive..
But its really RAM hungry.... even with 256, we may feel the delay...
It detected the power management, which many distributions failed to do 
till now... (for my laptop)...
it also detected each and every hardware exactly...
By saying exactly , I mean to say,
for example, I have a ALi 5451 Sound card..
but it showed it as HP's 5451 ALi sond card.. and like wise...
i wondered how it could detect that it was HP's...
and similarly for other hardware...
but it didnt install 3D Accleration support for my ATI RADEON 340M 
graphic card... in fact, till now, non of the distri did that... but i 
heard that suse is doing that..
ok thats it for now...
May be it will work more better on desktops...
bye

About CIOSA :-
=============

CIOSA (Confederation of Indian Organisations for Service and Advocacy)
is a collaborative forum for non-profit organisations, which brings
NGOs, socially motivated individuals and corporate houses on to a
common platform for mutually beneficial relationships by helping,
learning and sharing knowledge, resources and time. Non-profit
organizations remain the central focus of CIOSA. As of now there are
120 NGOs 5 corporates and 43 individuals in our network.

CIOSA Members:

1. CIOSA has member groups of varied causes. NGOs working for 
   Children, Women, Old, Disabled, etc...
2. From both urban and rural.
3. 80% of them are small and medium size group.
4. Not many are computer savvy. *****
5. Have problem with English.

What we Intend to achieve:

1. How FOSS can help us in communication, and as alternate to
   optimise their resource.
2. Tamil search or interfaces.

Volunteers List:

1. Hariram
2. Sakthi
3. Sudharshan
4. Bharathi

We need another 2 or 3 volunteers.

Volunteers, Kindly mail back to the list with the topic.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Oct 14 21:30:10 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Oct 14 21:26:14 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (REDIRECTIONS)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510142129430.9532-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

LinuxLinks.com is a big collection of Linux related site Links.
URL: http://www.linuxlinks.com/

One Day One Command 
===================

<, >, >>, | --  Redirection Operators.

Summary:

By using some special notation, we can redirect the output of many
commands to files, devices, even to the input of other commands and
pass the output of one command as input to another command. There are
3 Type redirections are available in shell:
 
1) Standard Output, 2) Standard Input and 3) Pipe

Examples:

$ ls > MyFile -- Redirecting the std output of 'ls' to a file.

$ ls >> MyFile -- Append the redirected 'ls' output to a file.

$ ls NoDir 2> MyFile -- Redirect the std errors to a file. (TRY: Just
                        remove the 2 and check the output).

$ touch a b -- Create 2 dummy file for testing.

$ ls a b c d > MyFile 2>&1 -- Redirect both std output and std error 
                              to a file.

$ sort < NameList -- Redirect the file 'NameList' as the input to the 
                     sort command.

$ sort < NameList > file -- Same as above. But here output is also
                            redirected to file.

$ ls -1 | sort | less -- Output of 'ls' is piped to 'sort' as an input
                    & output of 'sort' is piped to 'less' as an input.

Filter Programs performs operations on input and writes the result to
the standard output. Filters are very useful in redirection. Examples:
sort, tee, grep, less, head.

Read: info bash

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

> CIOSA (Confederation of Indian Organisations for Service and Advocacy)
> is a collaborative forum for non-profit organisations, which brings
> NGOs, socially motivated individuals and corporate houses on to a
> common platform for mutually beneficial relationships by helping,
> learning and sharing knowledge, resources and time. Non-profit
> organizations remain the central focus of CIOSA. As of now there are
> 120 NGOs 5 corporates and 43 individuals in our network.
>
> CIOSA Members:
>
> 1. CIOSA has member groups of varied causes. NGOs working for
> Children, Women, Old, Disabled, etc...
> 2. From both urban and rural.
> 3. 80% of them are small and medium size group.
> 4. Not many are computer savvy. *****
> 5. Have problem with English.
>
> What we Intend to achieve:
>
> 1. How FOSS can help us in communication, and as alternate to
> optimise their resource.
> 2. Tamil search or interfaces.
>
> Volunteers List:
>
> 1. Hariram
> 2. Sakthi
> 3. Sudharshan
> 4. Bharathi
>
> We need another 2 or 3 volunteers.
>
> Volunteers, Kindly mail back to the list with the topic.
>
> Bye :)

Date: Sat Oct 15 15:53:50 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Who governs the InterNet ??

	<a7a9a950510142313t5a8eeb8crc3c1a7192773b5bb@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120510150323u1ec1b8f8yc8ff7e77c9451070@mail.gmail.com>

On 10/15/05, Kris Dev <krisdev@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Unites States of America practically controls the whole world in almost
> every sphere of human activity!! No wonder they conrol the internet too
> and
> want to control it in future too!!


They control it because they funded all the research as well as the
actual implementation, as a DARPA project under the Pentagon. They
were under no obligation to turn it to civilian control under the ICANN
(overseen by the Dept. of Commerce), but they did so anyway because
the public benefit was much higher than the risk to U.S. national security.

Probably an American of Indian origin or
> any other origin could have created the internet for the world.


Yeah, and Ramar Pillai could have discovered the Theory of
Relativity - but he did not.

But just by
> being an American, they want to take control!!


No, they are in control because they paid for the research that
led to its development, almost of which was done by developers
and researchers in the U.S. Almost all of the content on the net
is also of U.S. origin.

Nobody is under any obligation to use the Internet - you can always
de-peer from the rest of the Internet today and build your own
local network with your own protocols, technology and domain names.
This is what some of the countries that want to take control of their
own networks want to do, and they are always free to do that.
Remember, nobody is under any obligation to route your packets
or to route packets to your network. The agreements are entirely voluntary.

Moreover, the value of isolated networks would be close to zero, by
Metcalfe's Law (the effectiveness of a network grows quadratically
with the number of vertices).

-Siva

Oh, if you WANT China or Iran controlling the Internet,...

against the glorious ideology of the People's Republic.

Iran would probably want separate Internets for men and women or something...

But I have a fundamental question for everyone: What exactly is "control" of 
the Net? Controlling the assignment of IPs? Controlling the rootservers? 
Control over domain names? With all of these being as distributed as they 
are, it's hard for me to see how they could ever be controlled by any one 
country. So, what do they want to control?

> > want to control it in future too!!
>
>
> They control it because they funded all the research as well as the
> actual implementation, as a DARPA project under the Pentagon. They
> were under no obligation to turn it to civilian control under the ICANN
> (overseen by the Dept. of Commerce), but they did so anyway because
> the public benefit was much higher than the risk to U.S. national
> security.
>
> Probably an American of Indian origin or
> > any other origin could have created the internet for the world.
>
>
> Yeah, and Ramar Pillai could have discovered the Theory of
> Relativity - but he did not.
>
> But just by
> > being an American, they want to take control!!
>
>
> No, they are in control because they paid for the research that
> led to its development, almost of which was done by developers
> and researchers in the U.S. Almost all of the content on the net
> is also of U.S. origin.
>
> Nobody is under any obligation to use the Internet - you can always
> de-peer from the rest of the Internet today and build your own
> local network with your own protocols, technology and domain names.
> This is what some of the countries that want to take control of their
> own networks want to do, and they are always free to do that.
> Remember, nobody is under any obligation to route your packets
> or to route packets to your network. The agreements are entirely
> voluntary.
>
> Moreover, the value of isolated networks would be close to zero, by
> Metcalfe's Law (the effectiveness of a network grows quadratically
> with the number of vertices).
>
> -Siva
>
>

On 10/15/05, Kris Dev <krisdev@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> They do what they do, because they cannot live in isolation! They do it
> for their benefit.
>
> On 10/15/05, Sivasankar Chander <siva.ilugc@gmail.com> wrote:
> >
> >
> > Nobody is under any obligation to use the Internet - you can always
> >  de-peer from the rest of the Internet today and build your own
> > local network with your own protocols, technology and domain names.
> > This is what some of the countries that want to take control of their
> > own networks want to do, and they are always free to do that.
> > Remember, nobody is under any obligation to route your packets
> > or to route packets to your network. The agreements are entirely
> > voluntary.
> >
>
In this context, check out this news item:

http://www.lightreading.com/document.asp?doc_id=82346

A dispute between backbone providers Cogent and Level 3 resulted in
Level 3 de-peering Cogent, leaving most of the Cogent network inaccessible
to the rest of the net.

Something similar to this can easily happen to all Internet access in India
-
if FLAG and a few of the companies that own the undersea fibre capacity
decide
to de-peer BSNL, Reliance, Bharti and a few other Indian ISPs, the Internet
in India will effectively become a large LAN and nothing else.

The reason that peering works is that it (normally) benefits both parties
to honour the peering agreement. If either party wants out, the agreement
breaks. It only works in your favour if you're willing to cooperate -
a lot like the GPL in SW development.

If you want to have your own net under your own control, you are always
welcome to do so, but you'll derive little or no benefit from it if nobody
accepts your packets or delivers packets to you.

-Siva

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Sat Oct 15 20:49:38 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Sat Oct 15 20:44:44 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (ASPELL)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510152048150.13672-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Linus Torvalds creator of the Linux Kernel.
URL: http://www.cs.helsinki.fi/~torvalds

One Day One Command 
===================

aspell -- Spell Checker

Summary:

Aspell can either be used as a library or as an independent spell
checker. Its main feature is suggesting possible replacements for a
misspelled word. Aspell can also easily check documents in UTF-8
without having to use a special dictionary.

Examples:

$ aspell -- Show Help/Usage message.

$ aspell conf -- Show ASpell configuration details.

$ aspell -l -- Start typing some words and Press Ctrl+D then aspell 
               list all misspelled words from that text.

$ aspell -c MyFile -- Run Spell checker over MyFile and Give a list of
                      replacement work for the misspelled words.

Read: man aspell or /usr/share/doc/aspell-xyz/
                 or http://aspell.sourceforge.net/

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

webpages you wouldn't think to search for.

On 10/16/05, Toufeeq Hussain <toufeeqh@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> S.Ramaswamy wrote:
> StumbleUpon
> (
> https://addons.mozilla.org/extensions/moreinfo.php?id=138&application=firefox
> )
> is a OSS Firefox extension which does the whole collaborative
> browsing/sharing/peer reviewing thing.
>
> Extension Description (from mozilla.org <http://mozilla.org>)
> StumbleUpon lets you "channelsurf" the best-reviewed sites on the web.
> It is a collaborative surfing tool for browsing, reviewing and sharing
> great sites with like-minded people. This helps you find interesting
> webpages you wouldn't think to search for.


Simility is different from StumbleUpon

Simility uses "implicity" user rating. The user need not click on "I like
it" or any button for each of his favourite websites. We find his interests
based on his browsing patterns. Also the webpages are *automatically*
categorized, but in stumbleupon the users/reviewers has to do it manually.

As simility gains more users, the recommendations will be better than
before.

ILUGC (www.chennailug.org/wiki) in collaboration with
CIOSA (http://www.ciosa.org.in/) organized a GNU/Linux
workshop for NGOs on Sunday, October 16, 2005 at Ma
Foi Academy, Chennai.

openoffice, desktop applications, Internet
applications, multimedia on GNU/Linux. Thanks to
Prasanna (CIOSA) for taking the initiative, Asokan
Pichai (Ma Foi) for providing us with the facilites at
Ma Foi, Vamsee Kanakala (Ma Foi) for coordinating the
events.

Subject: [Ilugc] USB bluetooth dongle which works in Linux
In-Reply-To: <495e45120510112143y76cde3bfnd2ffe386753ed9d5@mail.gmail.com>
References: <654433ee0510092306h3c3e8d9due90fed6f6db2a0d5@mail.gmail.com>
	<495e45120510112143y76cde3bfnd2ffe386753ed9d5@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <654433ee0510161126n74e0e4ebw2ae83a24646a1a30@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,
     Well, first of all, thanks to everyone for their help/suggestions!!

      I finally decided to just take the risk and buy some random
bluetooth dongle! I went to mercy electronics(being rather lazy to
drive all the way down to ritchie street), I picked up a bluetooth
dongle for Rs.475, with no manufacturer name on the box, which I later
found out to be 'bluesoleil' or something.

     It worked great in linux - absolutely no setup required! Atleast
on ubuntu, I just had to install the bluez and gnome-bluetooth
packages, and I was up and running!! I could quite easily send and
recieve files from/to the phone!! Really cool!! And it required far
lesser setup when compared to windows, where it required quite a bit
of driver and weird package installing to get working. It seems that
atleast as far as bluetooth is concerned, windows has really pathetic
support - very few drivers come bundled by default, I had to use the
cd that came with the device and install some weird program it came
with to get the device working.

    Am very close to getting the python bluetooth console working!! :)
There are quite a few more hacks to explore as well, such as making
the phone use the internet connection available on the computer
instead of gprs and such!! Cool Stuff! Maybe a demo is in order in the
next meet!

--
Thanks and Regards,
shiva

Subject: [Ilugc] Adelphi Charter
Message-ID: <a8f990120510161927n5843bdd5h6d5cb0b31c6d536c@mail.gmail.com>

Britain's Royal Society for the encouragement of Arts, Manufactures
and Commerce (RSA),

http://www.rsa.org.uk/

which is a venerable 250-year old institution, has issued the Adelphi
Charter,
drafted by numerous eminent personalities, including a Nobel Laureate and
various legal luminaries, which links IP policy to public benefit:

[Adelphi Charter] http://www.ipcharter.org/

[Commission Members] http://www.ipcharter.org/group.asp

[Guardian]
http://education.guardian.co.uk/higher/comment/story/0,9828,1591467,00.html

[Economist]
http://www.economist.com/business/displayStory.cfm?story_id=5032375

Among other things, it recommends a ban on the issue of software patents and
business
and medical process patents.

1. Download the ntfs rpm from 
http://linux-ntfs.sourceforge.net/rpm/fedora3.html and install. Select 
the right rpm as instructed by this download page.

2. Your BIPAC 7000 ADSL USB Modem has been listed as supported modem in
   the accessrunner site in the given link:
   http://accessrunner.sourceforge.net/modems.shtml
   Try this driver. If the above driver does not work let me know. I 
have ADSL USB Modem
   (same conexant chipset as that of BIPAC 7000 - vendor id: 0x0572 and
   product id: 0xcb06) supplied by Airtel DSL Services working fine with 
some
   other driver I downloaded long back. It is working on both Redhat 8.0
   (kernel 2.4) and FC3 (kernel 2.6) just like that. Almost just install and
   no configuration except your ISP username and password through html
   interface. I think It should work for you also. This driver even works
   with Debian clones also.

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Mon Oct 17 12:32:05 2005
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy)
Date: Mon Oct 17 12:29:38 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] 2 linux distros in the same system
Message-ID: <43534C6D.2070707@tandbintl.com>

What I use to follow:

1. A big / (root) partition (of 5GB min)  to do my day to day work 
(browsing, development, mailing, photos,...) - here I use to install 
stable feature rich distro. A /home partition to store my downloads and 
personal files irrespective of distros. (I use to preserve this /home 
partition at any instant to store downloaded essential rpms/debs like 
USB Modem drivers, kernel sources,...)

2. Another / (root) partition to have a feel of other distro released 
then and there (this size can be small around 2 GB min). This distro 
won't have seperate /home.

3. A common swap partition.

4. Always installing grub on MBR, which will take care of existing other 
OS partition also. Easy to edit grub.conf.

5. In my experience just 10GB is enough to have two distros comfortably. 
Rest can go for other OS.

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy





From chakkaradeepcc at gmail.com  Mon Oct 17 12:40:03 2005
From: chakkaradeepcc at gmail.com (Chakkaradeep C.C.)
Date: Mon Oct 17 12:40:26 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] 2 linux distros in the same system
In-Reply-To: <43534C6D.2070707@tandbintl.com>
References: <43534C6D.2070707@tandbintl.com>
Message-ID: <fa9c07110510170010w79781bafxcdf02568339b1608@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

>>1. A big / (root) partition (of 5GB min) to do my day to day work
>>(browsing, development, mailing, photos,...) - here I use to install
>>stable feature rich distro. A /home partition to store my downloads and
>>personal files irrespective of distros. (I use to preserve this /home
>>partition at any instant to store downloaded essential rpms/debs like
>>USB Modem drivers, kernel sources,...)
 ok u can do this by installing normally...
 >>.2. Another / (root) partition to have a feel of other distro released
>>then and there (this size can be small around 2 GB min). This distro
>>won't have seperate /home.
 again partition and proceeed the installation, but do not install
bootloader here because u already have an bootloader installed by the first
distribution.
 >>4. Always installing grub on MBR, which will take care of existing other
>>OS partition also. Easy to edit grub.conf.

not always..as mentioned above, install the grub/lilo during the first
installation, that is, in the 1st step...now edit the grub.conf or
lilo.confto load the second linux distribution by adding the necessary
root,initrd
and kernel parameters. The root parameter in kernel will change according to
your distribution.
 Hope i made u clear...If at all any other method is available for the
above.i would be very happy to know :-).
 with regards,
C.C.Chakkaradeep

From toufeeqh at gmail.com  Mon Oct 17 15:14:16 2005
From: toufeeqh at gmail.com (Toufeeq Hussain)
Date: Mon Oct 17 15:14:30 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Which Kernel version has Reiserfs 4
In-Reply-To: <20051017092619.2663.qmail@webmail28.rediffmail.com>
References: <20051017092619.2663.qmail@webmail28.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <c293dd340510170244y62ffc009hf82fdbbd91733fbe@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Raj,

On 17 Oct 2005 09:26:19 -0000, RAJ <rajkumar_chunkymails@rediffmail.com>
wrote:
>
> Dear sir,
> Had anyone tried Reiserfs 4 filesystem , if so which kernel version has
> the support for this filesystem.


First,
No formalities on ILUGC.

Second,
None of the vanilla kernel sources on http://kernel.org have support for
Rieser 4, i.e Rieser 4 is not a part of the mainline kernet(yet).

You will need to get the vanilla source for 2.6.13 and patch it with the
Rieser 4 patch which can be obtained from Namesys(http://namesys.com/)

The other alternative is to hunt for patchsets which can give you Rieser 4 +
other goodies/fixes.The -mm patchset has Rieser 4 support merged in but it's
not suitable for production usage.

For more info on Rieser 4 http://www.namesys.com/v4/v4.html

-toufeeq

The fastest, safest and best Browser !!

> Subject:
> [Ilugc] 2 linux distros in the same system
> From:
> "T.KaruppuSwamy" <swamytk@tandbintl.com>
> Date:
> Mon, 17 Oct 2005 12:32:05 +0530
> To:
> Chennai Linux User's Group <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>
>
> To:
> Chennai Linux User's Group <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>
>
>
> What I use to follow:
>
> 1. A big / (root) partition (of 5GB min)  to do my day to day work 
> (browsing, development, mailing, photos,...) - here I use to install 
> stable feature rich distro. A /home partition to store my downloads 
> and personal files irrespective of distros. (I use to preserve this 
> /home partition at any instant to store downloaded essential rpms/debs 
> like USB Modem drivers, kernel sources,...)
>
> 2. Another / (root) partition to have a feel of other distro released 
> then and there (this size can be small around 2 GB min). This distro 
> won't have seperate /home.
>
> 3. A common swap partition.
>
> 4. Always installing grub on MBR, which will take care of existing 
> other OS partition also. Easy to edit grub.conf.
>
> 5. In my experience just 10GB is enough to have two distros 
> comfortably. Rest can go for other OS.
>
> Regards
> T.KaruppuSwamy
>
>
>
>
>
>

>>>1. A big / (root) partition (of 5GB min) to do my day to day work
>>>(browsing, development, mailing, photos,...) - here I use to install
>>>stable feature rich distro. A /home partition to store my downloads and
>>>personal files irrespective of distros. (I use to preserve this /home
>>>partition at any instant to store downloaded essential rpms/debs like
>>>USB Modem drivers, kernel sources,...)
>>>      
>>>
> ok u can do this by installing normally...
> >>.2. Another / (root) partition to have a feel of other distro released
>  
>
>>>then and there (this size can be small around 2 GB min). This distro
>>>won't have seperate /home.
>>>      
>>>
> again partition and proceeed the installation, but do not install
>bootloader here because u already have an bootloader installed by the first
>distribution.
> >>4. Always installing grub on MBR, which will take care of existing other
>  
>
>>>OS partition also. Easy to edit grub.conf.
>>>      
>>>
>
>not always..as mentioned above, install the grub/lilo during the first
>installation, that is, in the 1st step...now edit the grub.conf or
>lilo.confto load the second linux distribution by adding the necessary
>root,initrd
>and kernel parameters. The root parameter in kernel will change according to
>your distribution.
> Hope i made u clear...If at all any other method is available for the
>above.i would be very happy to know :-).
> with regards,
>C.C.Chakkaradeep

>On 17 Oct 2005 09:26:19 -0000, RAJ <rajkumar_chunkymails@rediffmail.com>
>wrote:
>  
>
>>Dear sir,
>>Had anyone tried Reiserfs 4 filesystem , if so which kernel version has
>>the support for this filesystem.
>>    
>>
>
>
>First,
>No formalities on ILUGC.
>
>Second,
>None of the vanilla kernel sources on http://kernel.org have support for
>Rieser 4, i.e Rieser 4 is not a part of the mainline kernet(yet).
>
>You will need to get the vanilla source for 2.6.13 and patch it with the
>Rieser 4 patch which can be obtained from Namesys(http://namesys.com/)
>
>The other alternative is to hunt for patchsets which can give you Rieser 4 +
>other goodies/fixes.The -mm patchset has Rieser 4 support merged in but it's
>not suitable for production usage.
>
>For more info on Rieser 4 http://www.namesys.com/v4/v4.html
>
>-toufeeq
>

On Mon, 2005-10-17 at 09:26 +0000, RAJ wrote:
> Dear sir,
>         Had anyone tried Reiserfs 4 filesystem , if so which kernel version has the support for this filesystem.
> 

AFAIK 2.6.x (upto 2.6.13) will support reiser4 with the namesys patch
applied... I suggest u try the archck patchset
(http://iphitus.loudas.com/archck.php) I found this patchset to be
really cool... the ck patch is supposed to be a performance
accelerator :-)

On Sun, 2005-10-16 at 17:45 +0530, Niranjan B wrote:
> Hi,
> I have installed windows xp in my SATA HDD and FC4 in ATA HDD.
> When i select windows in the OS selection screen it says NTLDR missing.
> But i have given the location of windows xp properly in grub which is
> /dev/sda1.

do you specify "/dev/sda1" in ur menu.lst (/boot/grub/menu.lst) file?
IIRC grub uses a different numbering in the format (hdx,y).. where x
denotes the hard disk number and y the partition number both starting
from 0.

<quote>
	title Windows XP
	rootnoverify (hd0,0)
	chainloader +1
</quote>

> So i need to change the boot device each time i need to go to windows xp.
> Please help me solve this problem. I am a beginner in Linux.
> Thanks.

On 10/17/05, Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Can some one pls explain what evil the 'controller' of the internet can
> commit?
>
>
It's possible to to censor content by making certain sites inaccessible by
making their IP addresses non-resolvable, or even worse, non-routable.
It's also conceivable that certain groups may be denied domains or
other net privileges based on their beliefs/ethnicity/nationality etc.
(i.e. preferential quotas, etc.). China, for instance, restricts general
access to Google and certain other search engines. There's certainly
scope for considerable degradation in the hands of a repressive
regime.

-Siva

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: MoM NGO meet
In-Reply-To: <200510171030.j9HAUBcf008443@mail25.atl.registeredsite.com>
References: <200510171030.j9HAUBcf008443@mail25.atl.registeredsite.com>
Message-ID: <4353AC50.8040504@ciosa.org.in>

Dear All

CIOSA in Collaboration with Indian linux users group chennai arranged
oneday workshop on open source softwares on 16th of October. 26 members
from 17 organisations attended the programme.Members were given hands on
training on

1. Intro about FOSS.
2. Intro about Open Office.
3. Intro about Browsers, Email Clients and Howto Search
   in the Internet
4. Local Language Interface Demo
5. Multimedia Application Demo
6. Simple Troubleshoot Tips

The programme started at 10.15 AM. Mr Raman gave an introduction to open
source software explaining its history, need, how effective the opensource
can satisfy all the needs of customers. Mr Bharathi gave a presentation on
open desktop and the open office,writer, calc and impressions. Members had
an hands on experience on these for nearly one and half hours. Post lunch
began at 1.45 Mr Hari demonstrated tamil language interface,its
applications. After this the volunteers explained how to use internet and
search facilities, and offered trouble shoot tips.


The volunteers offered the members to help them in the transition period.
and also provide list of service providers who can help them install.

The CDs will be sent to the members later by post. Any queries and help
can be coordinated through CIOSA.
The programme came to an end with the request to have follow up session
based on the feed back from the members and their requirements.

Members who attended were requested to give their feed back as early as
possible to help us have feedback sessions.

with regards

Prasanna
CIOS

> apt-get source <pkg-name>

In addition, you should put 'deb-src' entry in your
/etc/apt/sources.list file. It could be similar to the following
entry:

deb-src http://gd.tuwien.ac.at/opsys/linux/debian/ sid main

Depending on your current setup, you may modify it.

In /boot/grub/menu.lst the entry for windows xp was

rootnoverify(hd1,0)

and the corresponding entry for FC4 was

root(hd0,1)

I have installed my bootloader in the ATA hard disk.

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Tue Oct 18 12:07:07 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Tue Oct 18 12:07:24 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: dynamic dns not working
In-Reply-To: <2308fde20510172100y56120ac0n7298eb36b65a6412@mail.gmail.com>
References: <2308fde20510132055o3b683facv38a812dcce8841f8@mail.gmail.com>
	<a8f990120510140213u7306d7a3jafe740704ced4723@mail.gmail.com>
	<2308fde20510172100y56120ac0n7298eb36b65a6412@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120510172337o7c4b5496u92dcda181066c246@mail.gmail.com>

On 10/18/05, sami nathan <meetsami@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> i hve some hundreads of systems,
>
> with dns (static ) every time i hve manually edit whenever there is a
> change in ip address of host changes using dhcp.


You've got a seriously mis-configured LAN. The standard configuration
uses non-routable static or dynamically allocated IP addresses (say,
192.168.1.xxx) for all the machines on the LAN. The Gateway machine
has LAN-facing interface with a non-routable static IP address, and a
WAN-facing interface that uses whatever protocol your ISP mandates
(say DHCP/PPPoE). The Gateway machine performs NAT (Network
Address Translation), and sometimes other functions including
packet filtering, port forwarding, dns/http caching.

You do *not* manually edit or alter the configurations of any system
on the LAN each time your ISP-supplied IP address changes. The Gateway
takes care of everything when NAT is properly configured.

so if i have Dynamic DNS server then i may get rid this problem,


Dynamic DNS solves a different problem - how to make a system with
a Dynamic IP visible to the Internet from outside the LAN using only its
Fully-Qualified Domain Name (FQDN). Check out:

http://www.technopagan.org/dynamic/

-Siva

> recently installed Win Xp, whose bootloader has made the grub
> non-functional.I tried linux rescue method and the 'grub-install' command
> when executed said 'sbin\grub : not found'.

When you use the install CD and boot in the rescue mode the root file
system is searched and is mounted under /mnt/sysimage (IIRC).

Perform a chroot to /mnt/sysimage and then try grub-install.

Jayakumar K K

Hi

  First of all, thanks for the Help. But I still have some problem with these implementations.

1> vrrpd implemention:
   This is restricted to 1 VRRP instatnce per interface. This is not acceptible for me. I need more than one VRRP instance per insterface. Refer the section 4.2 in rfc 2338 for the example.

2> Keepalived implementation:

   They are supporting many instances per interfaces. But all instances are having the same MAC address. This is actually a violation from RFC. mac address of vrrp interface should be, 00:00:5e:00:01:{VRID} (refer section 7.3 of rfc 2338). so whenever the vrid changes, corresponding mac should also change

Muneer CH

From binand at gmail.com  Tue Oct 18 10:32:02 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Tue Oct 18 20:02:15 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] gpg.
In-Reply-To: <d05619590510180712m36d3ad3cna1197dd4887a8340@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d05619590510180712m36d3ad3cna1197dd4887a8340@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610510180732r3d95212dt@mail.gmail.com>

On 18/10/05, nava ladi <navalady@gmail.com> wrote:
> I have a small document.That is my personal one.I want to encrypt that
> and then i need to decrypt when i need.I heard about gpg encryption
> tool in linux.I have looked in web and man pages but i can not
> understand.I tryied as far as i can.I have installed gpg command.
>
> Can u pls tell me the simple step's to encrypt and decrypt and create a key.
> Let us take file is personal.txt.

If you are the only person who needs access to this doc, the procedure
is as simple as:

gpg -c personal.txt
(give a decent passphrase)

It will encrypt the file and store it in personal.txt.gpg. You should
delete personal.txt after that (shred -u personal.txt for reasonably
secure deletion).

When you want to read the file again, just:

gpg -d -o personal.txt personal.txt.gpg
(give the same passphrase as above)

That's all to it.

Caveats:

1. DO NOT forget the passphrase. If you follow the steps above and
then forget the passphrase, your personal.txt is as good as lost.

2. The above procedure is only good for personal encryption. If you
need to share encrypted and signed documents, you have to go through
the full GPG setup and documentation.

Binand
From sbharathi at midascomm.com  Tue Oct 18 20:57:27 2005
From: sbharathi at midascomm.com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Oct 18 20:52:53 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (PLAY)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510182056270.24119-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Learn about the History of UNIX and its clones.
URL: http://www.levenez.com/unix/

One Day One Command 
===================

play -- Play the sound file.

Summary:

Play different types of sound files from the command line. It is a
front end to the more general sox package. Normally, the play will
automatically try to detect the type and other parameters of the sound
file.

Examples:

$ play snd.wav -- Play the wave file.

$ play snd.aiff -- Play the AIFF file.

$ play snd.wav echo .5 .5 100 .5 -- Play with echo effect.

$ play snd.wav reverb 1 1000 333 333 333 333 -- Play with reverb 
                                                effect.

$ play -v 2 snd.wav -- Change the volume and play.

Read: man play

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Wed Oct 19 07:27:19 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Wed Oct 19 07:34:16 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Create new partition without extended partition
In-Reply-To: <4dc6c9040510181244r3ad8392eg30f9bef03c683bd2@mail.gmail.com>
References: <4dc6c9040510181244r3ad8392eg30f9bef03c683bd2@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120510181857y1828797fwb56e4d595822b8d0@mail.gmail.com>

On 10/19/05, Bhuvaneswaran <bhuvaneswaran@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> I've 40gb hd. I've used 30gb (win 2000 -> 10gb, rh9.0 -> 10 gb, debian
> gnu/linux -> 10gb) & swap. I wish to use remaining 10gb. The fact is,
> i havn't created extended partition.
>
> bluestar:~# fdisk -l
>
> Disk /dev/hda: 40.0 GB, 40007761920 bytes
> 240 heads, 63 sectors/track, 5168 cylinders
> Units = cylinders of 15120 * 512 = 7741440 bytes
>
> Device Boot Start End Blocks Id System
> /dev/hda1 * 1 1355 10243768+ c W95 FAT32 (LBA)
> /dev/hda2 1356 2709 10236240 83 Linux
> /dev/hda3 2710 2980 2048760 82 Linux swap / Solaris
> /dev/hda4 2981 4273 9775080 83 Linux


1) You should have created an extended partition (say /dev/hda2) and created
all the primary Linux partitions within that.

2) Your swap is too large - 1x the RAM size is sufficient, even if you want
to do suspend-to-disk.

3) One possible way around this to use partition-magic from windows, and
see if you can convert the windows primary partition into an extended
partition. Then move it to the end and merge it with the unused space,
then create additional partitions in the extended partition. There's always
the risk of losing data in the Windows partition.

4) The other way is to use a second hard drive and copy out the entire
Linux trees, and copy it back after re-adjusting the partitions.

-Siva

China in million pieces. No wonder, they can didctate terms to anyone!!!

billion citizens?

Kris Dev.

Kris Dev wrote:

> When will we ever learn to become more transparent and accountable to 
> our billion citizens?
>
Sorry if I'm taking this more OT, indeed, China is in an admirable 
postion today. With a authoritarian regime, things like discipline are 
easier to enforce. I don't doubt it's manufacturing muscle, I'm sure 
India would find it difficult to match it. But do the ends justify the 
means? Does it really matter that you're one of the most powerful 
countries on earth (economic or otherwise) when your citizens don't have 
most basic individual rights?

Democracy is much more messier, slower than 
dictatorship/authoritarianism. But, I'm much more comfortable living in 
a poor but free country than a rich but non-free country. Wow, I think 
I'm coming pretty near to a circular reference to FOSS ;-)

Vamsee.

Subject: [Ilugc] can't recover grub in a dual boot system
In-Reply-To: <BAY110-F7D86F9F1192ED2F330719BF700@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY110-F7D86F9F1192ED2F330719BF700@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <7c6561690510190456wd054f6exe5b2f8b08a6fb1b8@mail.gmail.com>

hi,

> I have not created the boot partion during the Red Hat os installation so
> use of Linux Rescue disk failed to detect the Linux partition in my
> computer.


don't mind if ur partitons are not mounted by default.

if u know the partition names u can just mount them like this,

mkdir /test
mount /dev/hda5 /test
vi /test/boot/grub/grub.conf

incase u don't have the device files create them using mknod as follows,

mknod /dev/hda b 3 0
mknod /dev/hda1 b 3 1
.
.
.
mknod /dev/hdb b 3 64
....
mknod /dev/hdc b 22 0
.....
mknod /dev/hdd b 22 64

remenber u need not create all the above
i just mentoned them for ur refernce.

hope this helped u.
bye
regards,
kiran
From saikiranrgda at gmail.com  Wed Oct 19 17:34:04 2005
From: saikiranrgda at gmail.com (Sai Kiran)
Date: Wed Oct 19 17:34:16 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Create new partition without extended partition
In-Reply-To: <4dc6c9040510181244r3ad8392eg30f9bef03c683bd2@mail.gmail.com>
References: <4dc6c9040510181244r3ad8392eg30f9bef03c683bd2@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <7c6561690510190504y413d1187pc051b73095e16587@mail.gmail.com>

hi,

wht i suggest is delete the swap in fdisk and then create a new
extended partition with starting cylinder  as 4273 and till the end of
the disk.

once u do this u can create a large logical partition and copy the
data from /dev/hda4 ( current part no.) to one of the logical and
delete it too sort of backup. then create a new one with starting
cylinder as 2710 to a size of ur choice and then restore the dump tht
u have taken into the logical partition.

then u can delete the logiccal partition and recreate to restore symetry.


do this at ur own risk.

regards,
kiran.

From praveen at symonds.net  Wed Oct 19 18:05:12 2005
From: praveen at symonds.net (Praveen Kumar)
Date: Wed Oct 19 18:06:48 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] can't recover grub in a dual boot system
In-Reply-To: <BAY110-F7D86F9F1192ED2F330719BF700@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY110-F7D86F9F1192ED2F330719BF700@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <43563D80.1020609@symonds.net>

Pradeep Kumar wrote:

> I have not created the boot partion during the Red Hat os installation 
> so use of Linux Rescue disk failed to detect the Linux partition in my 
> computer.
> Any ideas how to mount the linux partition and re-modify the grub.conf 
> file to default values?

Absence of boot partition is not an issue. I think your Linux is on a 
non-ext3 partition, maybe reiserfs, jfs or xfs. In that case you need to 
pass the appropriate argument along with 'linux rescue' command line of 
your rescue/install disk. Also the rescue/install disc that you are 
using may be of a older version of the distro.

Simple way is to use a live CD (Maybe ubuntu) and modify the GRUB conf.

HTH.

-- 
Praveen Kumar
http://www.praveen.ws

What do mean here, DHCP is for dynamically assigning IP address?


>
>
> here 10.1.1.50 <http://10.1.1.50> is my proxy server.When i set
> 10.255.240.102 <http://10.255.240.102> i can not
> get the internet connection.For other values of IP address i can get
> it right..

With other IP address set other than 10.255.240.102 <http://10.255.240.102>,
can you ping 10.255.240.102 <http://10.255.240.102> ;-) your neighbor could
be using that.

If you are saying your university uses dhcp for IP assignment, first check
the range. If 10.255.240.102 <http://10.255.240.102> is the range , the dhcp
server could have allocated it to other machine for a given leased time.

If you need a static IP within your network, you got to check with your
admin over there, get details and if you still have problems, let us know.

>
> One Day One Command
> ===================
>
> play -- Play the sound file.
>
> Summary:
>
> Play different types of sound files from the command line. It is a
> front end to the more general sox package. Normally, the play will
> automatically try to detect the type and other parameters of the sound
> file.
>
> Examples:
>
> $ play snd.wav -- Play the wave file.
>
> $ play snd.aiff -- Play the AIFF file.
>
> $ play snd.wav echo .5 .5 100 .5 -- Play with echo effect.
>
> $ play snd.wav reverb 1 1000 333 333 333 333 -- Play with reverb
> effect.
>
> $ play -v 2 snd.wav -- Change the volume and play.
>
> Read: man play
>
> HTH :)
> --
> Bharathi S
> ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

> From: Sivasankar Chander <siva.ilugc@gmail.com>
> Subject: Re: [Ilugc] Create new partition without extended partition
> To: Bhuvaneswaran <bhuvaneswaran@gmail.com>
> Cc: ilugc <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>
> Message-ID:
> <a8f990120510181857y1828797fwb56e4d595822b8d0@mail.gmail.com>
> Content-Type: text/plain; charset=ISO-8859-1
>
> On 10/19/05, Bhuvaneswaran <bhuvaneswaran@gmail.com> wrote:
> >
> >
> > I've 40gb hd. I've used 30gb (win 2000 -> 10gb, rh9.0 -> 10 gb, debian
> > gnu/linux -> 10gb) & swap. I wish to use remaining 10gb. The fact is,
> > i havn't created extended partition.
> >
> > bluestar:~# fdisk -l
> >
> > Disk /dev/hda: 40.0 GB, 40007761920 bytes
> > 240 heads, 63 sectors/track, 5168 cylinders
> > Units = cylinders of 15120 * 512 = 7741440 bytes
> >
> > Device Boot Start End Blocks Id System
> > /dev/hda1 * 1 1355 10243768+ c W95 FAT32 (LBA)
> > /dev/hda2 1356 2709 10236240 83 Linux
> > /dev/hda3 2710 2980 2048760 82 Linux swap / Solaris
> > /dev/hda4 2981 4273 9775080 83 Linux
>
>
> 1) You should have created an extended partition (say /dev/hda2) and
> created
> all the primary Linux partitions within that.
>
> 2) Your swap is too large - 1x the RAM size is sufficient, even if you
> want
> to do suspend-to-disk.
>
> 3) One possible way around this to use partition-magic from windows, and
> see if you can convert the windows primary partition into an extended
> partition. Then move it to the end and merge it with the unused space,
> then create additional partitions in the extended partition. There's
> always
> the risk of losing data in the Windows partition.
>
> 4) The other way is to use a second hard drive and copy out the entire
> Linux trees, and copy it back after re-adjusting the partitions.
>
> -Siva
>
> ------------------------------
>

From binand at gmail.com  Wed Oct 19 11:57:45 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Wed Oct 19 21:27:55 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] DHCP Servers List
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510191901270.27112-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510191901270.27112-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610510190857i1bbf92bav@mail.gmail.com>

On 19/10/05, Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@midascomm.com> wrote:
> Is it possible to get the list of DHCP Servers address on the current
> network ??  I tried to find it using TCP/UDP port scan technique. But
> No luck :(

Usually there is only one DHCP server in a given subnet. If you
suspect there are more, some of the things you can try are:

1. Scan the subnet on port 67/udp using Nmap: nmap -sU -p 67
192.168.100.0/24 (you will need root privileges to run nmap -sU).

2. Send out test DHCP requests and look at the IPs responding. Perl is
good - look up Net::DHCP or Net::DHCPClient on CPAN.

3. Try something like dhcp_probe -
http://www.net.princeton.edu/software/dhcp_probe/

Binand

From ashwin.chn at gmail.com  Wed Oct 19 21:56:05 2005

On 10/19/05, Parthan SR <parth.technofreak@gmail.com> wrote:
>    Dear Linuxians,
>    I tried instaling mpg321 player using its RPM
>    mpg321-0.2.10-6.2.fc4.i386.rpm. But when the RPM checked the dependencies
>    it said the following two packages were needed but not found, so i couldnt
>    proceed installing mpg321. The packages are: libid3tag.so.O and
>    libmod.so.O. Where will i find these two and how to install them so i cam
>    install mpg321 ??

Hi,
   Don't try installing through rpm -ivh <package> . It gets you into
dependency problem like the one you are in. If you have all the
dependecies and know the right order then the rpm cmd would be a easy
way. Otherwise yum is a better soloution. You need to have root access
to use yum. For which you can su - or sudo or login as root and issue
the cmd
yum install <package name>
If you don't get the software you need with this cmd the try adding
more repositories to /etc/yum.repo.d/ directory. I assume that you are
using redhat based distro. If not there must be similar software eg.
apt-get.

HTH

--ashwin

Does it really matter that you're one of the largest democracies on earth
(developing for the last 58 years, when most citizens don't have most basic
essentials for living, except the so called freedom of speech?

Our present form of Democracy is hypocrisy and worse than
dictatorship/authoritarianism. But, I'm much more comfortable living in a
poor but free country than a rich but non-free country, as I have the
minimum comforts in life, which are denied to most of my countrymen as true
merit has very little merit and only connections speak.

I challenge the powers that be - Politicians, bureaucracy, judiciary,
businessmen and rich to give up currency circulation and make all
transactions transparent on the web. You can see a truly developed India,
better than China.

From: Matt Zimmerman <mdz@ubuntu.com>
Date: Oct 19, 2005 11:55 PM
Subject: Ubuntu 5.10 Server
To: ubuntu-announce@lists.ubuntu.com

The Ubuntu team is proud to announce Ubuntu 5.10 Server, the first
release of Ubuntu designed especially for server environments.
Like the standard desktop Ubuntu, it occupies a single CD. However,
it is distinguished by the following features:

* Includes server-oriented kernels with out-of-the-box
automatic support for multiprocessor systems
* Includes a wide variety of popular server applications
such as apache, mysql, postgresql, php, zope, openldap,
bind, samba, all on the single CD, ready for installation
* A slim default installation, occupying just 400 megabytes:
add only the software you need, for a clean, maintainable
configuration.
* Provides no desktop environment (GNOME, KDE, etc.) by default
* Safe and text-oriented boot mode for better clarity and
infinite justice on boot.

The default installation is secure by design, with no network ports active
after installation and access to free security updates activated. Network
services are activated only when explicitly installed.

As always, it's supported with regular releases, a commitment to
security updates for 18 months after each release and professional
technical support from many companies around the world.

For more information about the new features shared with Ubuntu 5.10,
see the Ubuntu 5.10 announcement at

http://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-announce/2005-October/000038.html

From bhuvaneswaran at gmail.com  Wed Oct 19 15:29:55 2005
From: bhuvaneswaran at gmail.com (Bhuvaneswaran)
Date: Thu Oct 20 04:00:03 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Create new partition without extended partition
In-Reply-To: <7c6561690510190504y413d1187pc051b73095e16587@mail.gmail.com>
References: <4dc6c9040510181244r3ad8392eg30f9bef03c683bd2@mail.gmail.com>
	<7c6561690510190504y413d1187pc051b73095e16587@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4dc6c9040510191529u4435f544ga9c313b9e4005f13@mail.gmail.com>

> wht i suggest is delete the swap in fdisk and then create a new
> extended partition with starting cylinder  as 4273 and till the end of
> the disk.
>
> once u do this u can create a large logical partition and copy the
> data from /dev/hda4 ( current part no.) to one of the logical and
> delete it too sort of backup. then create a new one with starting
> cylinder as 2710 to a size of ur choice and then restore the dump tht
> u have taken into the logical partition.
>
> then u can delete the logiccal partition and recreate to restore symetry.

Cool! I did and it worked! Thankx much.
What i did is slightly different though. I deleted the swap partition
(hda3), created new extended partition starting 4274 to 5168 (hda3)
and created two new logical partitions (hda5 & hda6). I set hda5 as
swap, hda6 as ext3 and sacrificed old swap (2GB)!

From toufeeqh at gmail.com  Thu Oct 20 20:33:45 2005
From: toufeeqh at gmail.com (Toufeeq Hussain)
Date: Thu Oct 20 15:04:05 2005
Subject: [ilugc]USB drive umount problem
In-Reply-To: <73a10bbf0510200115r798ea18eh679d8d4e64dbcc0b@mail.gmail.com>
References: <73a10bbf0510200115r798ea18eh679d8d4e64dbcc0b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4357B1D1.50106@gmail.com>

Arpit Sud wrote:
> hi,
> 
> I have the following entry in fstab
> /dev/sda1   /mnt/sda1     vfat   rw,group,noauto,sync     0    0
> 
> After mounting my usb drive, the
> $ umount /dev/sda1
> gives "Device or Resource busy"

that should be `umount /mnt/sda1` not '\dev\sda1'.
/dev/sda1 is the device file.
/mnt/sda1 is the mount point.umount will un-mount a mount point.
For more info, read the man pages.

> # fuser /mnt/sda1
> gives the pid of "famd"
> 
> The man page of "famd" says that the configuration file for famd is
> /etc/fam.conf
> 
> $ less /etc/fam.conf
> less: No such file or directory
> 
> The only way for me umount is to shut down.

If all else fails try `umount -f /mnt/sda1`.

HTH,
toufeeq

> that should be `umount /mnt/sda1` not '\dev\sda1'.
> /dev/sda1 is the device file.
> /mnt/sda1 is the mount point.umount will un-mount a mount point.
> For more info, read the man pages.


doesn't matter because umount looks up the values from the /etc/mtab.
so it doesn't matter whether u umount using device named or mount points.

regards,
kiran

On 10/20/05, veeraa bose <veeraaexp@gmail.com> wrote:

>
> the error message is rncd : connction refused
>


do u have this in the named.conf   ....

controls {
        inet 127.0.0.1 allow { localhost; } keys { rndckey; };
};


the above line line the  localhost control the named server.

and also check if u have the localloop back running.

regards,
kiran

Sai Kiran wrote:
> hi,
> 
> 
>>Yes, you're right.
>>Just one problem,umounting using the device name will fail when the
>>device is mounted on multiple mount points.
> 
> as far as i know u can only mount a device once. but rather u can bind
> an already existing directory into another dir.
> 
> how do u mount the same device in two places.

Basically, mutiple mount points can exist which will point to the same 
block device.

However for this to occur I guess there should be no entry in /etc/mtab 
which can be done through the "-n" switch of mount which prevents an 
entry to be written in /etc/mtab.

-toufeeq

govt perspective.

about calling through a phone device attached to the internet port?

vonage charges 17 cents a minute, so they probably are paying all the
taxes to Indian govt.

connects into an ethenrnet port. A phone can be plugged into the modem.

vONAGE at home..

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Oct 21 10:58:34 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Oct 21 10:52:48 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: FSFE: Early comment on new MS Shared Source Licenses
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510211053420.2632-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

-------- Forwarded Message --------
To: press-release at fsfeurope dot org
Date: Wed, 19 Oct 2005 13:44:07 -0200

FSFE: Early comment on new Microsoft Shared Source Licenses

"Since we so rarely have opportunity to say something positive about
Microsoft, let me begin by congratulating them", says Georg Greve,
president of Free Software Foundation Europe. "Microsoft finally seems
to have made a step forward on their long march towards giving their
users freedom: of the five licenses published, our cursory first
analysis suggests that two of them indeed fulfill the Free Software
Definition."

According to FSFEs first glance, the "Microsoft Permissive License"
(Ms-PL) and "Microsoft Community License" (Ms-CL) both appear to
satisfy the four freedoms that define Free Software. In particular:
The Ms-CL also appears to implement a variation of the Copyleft idea,
which was first implemented by the GNU General Public License (GPL).

Given previous Microsoft statements about the Copyleft approach and in
particular the GNU GPL as 'viral', 'cancerous' and 'communist', seeing
Microsoft now publish licenses applying the very same principles seems
quite an evolution.

Naturally, it is not the publication of licenses, but the publication
of software under a Free Software license, that gives people freedom:

It is indeed not very useful if every company, administration or
author publishes their own license; so it would have been preferrable
if Microsoft had made the decision to use the GNU General Public
License (GPL) and Lesser General Public License (LGPL) for its Shared
Source program.

Far more than 50% of Free Software worldwide is published under these
licenses, they are very well-known and people trust them for good
reason.

"Microsoft has walked a mile and is now standing mere inches from the
GNU (L)GPL: We fully understand that Microsoft is first trying to get
the nail of its little toe wet in the Free Software community, and we
welcome that," continues Greve. "But in the course of time we would
prefer to see Microsoft join the large global community of commercial
GNU (L)GPL vendors."

"For now it will be good if Microsoft starts relicensing its portfolio
under the Ms-PL or Ms-CL; but we still have to warn people to be
careful about the 'Shared Source' label and look at the specific
licenses: The other three licenses of the Shared Source program are
clearly proprietary and obviously do not qualify as Free Software."
Greve finishes.

The Free Software Foundations will need more time to study all these
licenses and their interactions with other licenses in depth, so this
is not a final evaluation -- and the final evaluation may as well
reveal problems that were not visible at first sight.

Microsoft still has a long way to go, but for now it seems they made a
step in the right direction, and the Free Software Foundation Europe
hopes they will keep it up.

About the Free Software Foundation Europe:

The Free Software Foundation Europe (FSFE), founded 2001, is a
charitable non-governmental organisation dedicated to all aspects of
Free Software in Europe. Access to software determines who may
participate in a digital society. The the Freedoms to use, copy,
modify and redistribute software - as described in the Free Software
definition - allow equal participation in the information age.
Creating awareness for these issues, securing Free Software
politically and legally, and giving people Freedom by supporting
development of Free Software are central issues of the FSFE.

Arpit Sud wrote:
>>If all else fails try `umount -f /mnt/sda1`.
> 
> 
> I had already tried this but this didn't work.
Does umount fail in *all* cases ?

What happend when you just plug in the device,perform no operations and 
then un-mount it ?

Write operations to block devices are done asynchronously.When you 
un-mount a device it performs the write operations.So I suggest once you 
copy something on to the device, wait for some time for the write 
operation to complete and then umount it.

-toufeeq

On 10/21/05, Toufeeq Hussain <toufeeqh@gmail.com> wrote:
> Arpit Sud wrote:
> What happend when you just plug in the device,perform no operations and
> then un-mount it ?
I think you meant plug in the device, [mount it], perform no
operations and umount it.
Yes, i have done this. I still get the Device busy error.

>
> Write operations to block devices are done asynchronously.

In the fstab entry i gave in my first mail, the options were given as
'sync'. So write operations are not async.

>wait for some time for the write
>operation to complete and then umount it.
If the mount option is async, i had to wait around a minute while
umounting, so that the data is synced. In order to avoid waiting i
changed the mount option to sync.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Sat Oct 22 12:05:08 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Sat Oct 22 11:59:44 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (REC)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510221204110.8473-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

SimpleKDE: A LightWeight, Clean and User-Friendly Desktop Environment
based on KDE. URL: http://www.simplekde.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

rec -- Record the Audio in a file.

Summary:

'rec' program help us record the audio input in different types (wav,
cdr, aiff, gsm, ogg, snd, raw, ..) of sound files from the command
line.

Examples:

$ rec myFile.wav -- Record the audio in WAV format.

$ rec myFile.cdr -- Record the audio in CD Audio file format.

$ rec -c 2 myFile.wav -- Record the audio in WAV format.

$ rec -r 44100 myFile.wav -- Record the audio in WAV format with high 
                             sample rate to get good quality.

Read: man rec

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Sun Oct 23 17:40:06 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Sun Oct 23 17:34:06 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: [Electronics Expert Volunteer Needed]
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510231734060.17808-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

---------- Forwarded message ----------
From: Nagarjuna G. <nagarjun at gnowledge dot org>

Fred is looking for a hardware hacker to fix some problem for a free
wireless infrastructure developement, any one can find a solution?
Write to fred if you need further information, with a cc to me.

----- Message from Fred Pook <fredpook@gmail.com> -----

> From: Fred Pook <fredpook at gmail dot com>
> Subject: electronics expert volunteer needed

> Since we are allowed to use 1 Watt RF output on the 2.4 Ghz
> frequency in India. And most Wi-Fi consumer products that we are
> using only output about 80mW, I went on a search for a low-cost RF
> amplifier. I found:

> http://www.fairchildsemi.com/news/2004/0407/rmpa2455.html

> chosen by broadcom (the producer of the chipset used in WRT54G and
> Asus) as the basis of an 2.4Ghz amplifier. So being Dutch and bold I
> just went on an ordered 10 of them here:

> http://www.digikey.com/scripts/dksearch/dksus.dll?KeywordSearch?Keywords=RMPA2455%20fairchild&site=us

> to my surprise they arrived with no problem. Now this IC is very
> small 3 X 3mm with 16 tiny surface mounting contacts and it needs
> some supporting capacitors etc all describe in the datasheet here:

> http://www.fairchildsemi.com/ds/RM/RMPA2455.pdf

> Do you know any electronics hackers in India who can put this
> together for us? And how to get these tiny little IC's to him? To
> have some extra RF output will make our wireless life a lot easier
> since we don't have to worry to much about cable and plug loss and
> it can keep the design of the antenna much smaller and lower-cost.
> Now higher output doesn't solve every problem on long range Wi-Fi
> connections (fresnel zone clearance is the big one) but it did
> wonders for the Djursland project after they got 1Watt 802.11a
> equipment.

----- End forwarded message -----

Bye :)

Bharathi S

200 MB of hard disk (if installed).

requires 16 MB of RAM and 16 MB of hard disk.

The various LRP/LEAF/LOAF distros are even smaller. They must be
smoking something potent if they think that Minix 3 is going to work for
resource-limited embedded applications.

> PART II: if i install unstable version of debian sarge 3.1, can i apply some stable updates to it from the net? 
> regards

the unstable version of debian is called "Sid" and testing version is
called "Etch". If you do a complete dist-upgrage to debian sid, then you
will no longer hold relevance to security updates since you will be
working on an "unstable environment" and will have access too bleeding
edge software. However personally, i use Debian Sid and have not found
it to be the least bit "unstable" ;-) unless you mean for your system to
be a server, i would suggest you do an "apt-get update && apt-get
dist-upgrade" and changing all your "stable" to "unstable"
in /etc/apt/sources.list (provided you have a good net connection of
course)

> g.ramanathan
>

Prashanth Mohan <prashmohan@gmail.com> writes:
> sorry but I am quite ignorant abt the topic of kernel :-) but
> wouldnt it make sense that a micro kernel need more resources
> since it needs to keep passing messages between the mdoules?

No., actually this depends on the implementation and the features
provided by a Microkernel. A microkernel such as the Mach takes
more memory and resources than a normal UNIX. However, the L4 is
lean and simple and powerful. So., the whole thing is about design
and implementation.

From sbharathi at midascomm.com  Mon Oct 24 21:44:32 2005
From: sbharathi at midascomm.com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Oct 25 09:38:30 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (STAT)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510242144030.23817-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

LinuxPrinting.org is having lot of resources to help with printing
under Free OS like GNU/Linux and the BSDs or commercial UNIX-like
systems. URL: http://www.linuxprinting.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

stat -- Show the File/File-System status.

Summary:

stat shows the detailed and formatted information about the file or
file-system status, like Size, Blocks, Time Access/Modify/Change etc...

Examples:

$ stat myfile -- Show the status of myfile.

$ stat -f myfile -- Show the status of the File-System, where this file 
                    is resided.

$ stat -t myfile -- Show the status in plain/terse form.

$ stat -c "%A %U %G %s %Y %n" * -- Custom format (ls like) output.

Read: man stat

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Tue Oct 25 16:41:58 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Wed Oct 26 00:52:04 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] JavaScript bug in Math functions in Mozilla 64 bit versions
Message-ID: <435E12FE.7020902@gmail.com>

JavaScript functions Math.pow and Math.log in 64 bit versions of 
Mozilla/Firefox return incorrect values - take care if your scripts use 
them.

-Ramanraj K

<html>
<script language="javascript">
<!--
function test_math(){
// check if Math functions return correct values
var x = Math.log(10);    // should return 1
alert(x);                // 64 bit Moz returns 1.9<snip>e51
var y = Math.pow(10, 2); // should return 100
alert(y);                // 64 bit Moz returns 0
}
//-->
</script>
<body onload="test_math()">
Testing Math.pow
</html>

From binand at gmail.com  Wed Oct 26 05:50:11 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Wed Oct 26 15:20:19 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] EOF in linux
In-Reply-To: <7253b3d60510260229t5cdd4893m123101e7419a30d1@mail.gmail.com>
References: <6ae8cb56.5099783c.81a0b00@mail.tataelxsi.co.in>
	<20051025063753.GA4442@localhost>
	<7253b3d60510250308q4339ed02o85820775b5cffc38@mail.gmail.com>
	<200510260949.43343.trshash84@gmail.com>
	<d2a92d610510260056g2a9a1d27u@mail.gmail.com>
	<7253b3d60510260229t5cdd4893m123101e7419a30d1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610510260250j1b8eab6eh@mail.gmail.com>

On 26/10/05, Natarajan K <knutties@gmail.com> wrote:
> > Even though theoretically it can be any signed char < 0.
>
> EOF isn't a char/int. It is just a condition (that there is nothing
> more to read) that is normally indicated with a return value of -1 by
> system calls.

First of all, system calls don't return EOF - stdio library functions
do. Even then, some stdio functions return other error indicators -
NULL, maybe - and the programmer is expected to check with feof() to
see if EOF actually happened.

As you say, EOF is a condition - that there is nothing more to read.
But it is ALSO the #define'd constant in stdio.h (and specified
somewhere in ISO C standard) which can be a char/int/whatever, and
represents the condition to the programmer. My (rather old) draft copy
of ISO C defines EOF as:

(EOF) expands to an integer constant expression,  with  type
          int  and  a  negative  value,  that  is  returned by several
          functions to indicate end-of-file, that is,  no  more  input
          from a stream.

Binand

> > mknod /dev/hda1 b 3 1
> > .
> > .
> > .
> > mknod /dev/hdb b 3 64
> > ....
> > mknod /dev/hdc b 22 0
> > .....
> > mknod /dev/hdd b 22 64

>Pradeep Kumar wrote:
>
> > I have not created the boot partion during the Red Hat os installation
> > so use of Linux Rescue disk failed to detect the Linux partition in my
> > computer.
> > Any ideas how to mount the linux partition and re-modify the grub.conf
> > file to default values?
>
>Absence of boot partition is not an issue. I think your Linux is on a
>non-ext3 partition, maybe reiserfs, jfs or xfs. In that case you need to
>pass the appropriate argument along with 'linux rescue' command line of
>your rescue/install disk. Also the rescue/install disc that you are
>using may be of a older version of the distro.
>
>Simple way is to use a live CD (Maybe ubuntu) and modify the GRUB conf.
>
>HTH.

> >
> > Learn about the History of UNIX and its clones.
> > URL: http://www.levenez.com/unix/
> >
> > One Day One Command
> > ===================
> >
> > play -- Play the sound file.
> >
> > Summary:
> >
> > Play different types of sound files from the command line. It is a
> > front end to the more general sox package. Normally, the play will
> > automatically try to detect the type and other parameters of the sound
> > file.
> >
> > Examples:
> >
> > $ play snd.wav -- Play the wave file.
> >
> > $ play snd.aiff -- Play the AIFF file.
> >
> > $ play snd.wav echo .5 .5 100 .5 -- Play with echo effect.
> >
> > $ play snd.wav reverb 1 1000 333 333 333 333 -- Play with reverb
> > effect.
> >
> > $ play -v 2 snd.wav -- Change the volume and play.
> >
> > Read: man play
> >
> > HTH :)
> > --
> > Bharathi S
> > ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/
> >

> > On 10/19/05, Bhuvaneswaran <bhuvaneswaran@gmail.com> wrote:
> > >
> > >
> > > I've 40gb hd. I've used 30gb (win 2000 -> 10gb, rh9.0 -> 10 gb, debian
> > > gnu/linux -> 10gb) & swap. I wish to use remaining 10gb. The fact is,
> > > i havn't created extended partition.
> > >
> > > bluestar:~# fdisk -l
> > >
> > > Disk /dev/hda: 40.0 GB, 40007761920 bytes
> > > 240 heads, 63 sectors/track, 5168 cylinders
> > > Units = cylinders of 15120 * 512 = 7741440 bytes
> > >
> > > Device Boot Start End Blocks Id System
> > > /dev/hda1 * 1 1355 10243768+ c W95 FAT32 (LBA)
> > > /dev/hda2 1356 2709 10236240 83 Linux
> > > /dev/hda3 2710 2980 2048760 82 Linux swap / Solaris
> > > /dev/hda4 2981 4273 9775080 83 Linux
> >
> >
> > 1) You should have created an extended partition (say /dev/hda2) and
> > created
> > all the primary Linux partitions within that.
> >
> > 2) Your swap is too large - 1x the RAM size is sufficient, even if you
> > want
> > to do suspend-to-disk.
> >
> > 3) One possible way around this to use partition-magic from windows, and
> > see if you can convert the windows primary partition into an extended
> > partition. Then move it to the end and merge it with the unused space,
> > then create additional partitions in the extended partition. There's
> > always
> > the risk of losing data in the Windows partition.
> >
> > 4) The other way is to use a second hard drive and copy out the entire
> > Linux trees, and copy it back after re-adjusting the partitions.
> >
> > -Siva
> >
> > ------------------------------
> >

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Oct 26 20:55:09 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Oct 26 20:48:00 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (CHATTR)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0510262054430.31469-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Linux.Org is designed to act as a central source of Linux information,
as a voice for the promotion and advocacy of the Linux based OS and
information about the contributors. URL: http://www.linux.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

chattr -- Change File Attributes on a Ext2 File System.

Summary:

Ext2 File System(FS) is providing few extra bit to set some special
attribute to each file in the FS. 'chattr' command is used to changes
the file's special attributes on a Ext2 FS.

Examples:

$ chattr +A myFile -- Don't change the Access time of this file.

$ chattr -V +A myFile -- Same as above. But show verbose output.

$ chattr +c myFile -- Save the file in compressed mode.

# chattr +i myFile -- Make the file as Read-Only.

$ chattr +s myFile -- Mark the file as secrete. During deletion its 
                      blocks are Zeroed.

$ chattr +u myFile -- Mark for undeletion. If this file is deleted, 
                      user can ask for undelete.

$ chattr +S myFile -- The changes in the file are written
                      synchronously on the disk.

# chattr -i myFile -- Remove the Read-Only Mark.

$ chattr =Ac myFile -- Set only A & c bit. Clear all other bits.

Read: man chattr

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Wed Oct 26 10:32:29 2005

Hi

--- Shakthi Kannan <cyborg4k@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Do you have to pass anything specific to the kernel
> on
> bootup?

Ok. I found out the parameters by pressing F1. You can
pass the following to boot,

  slax dbg

I also passed, "nohotplug nopcmcia" to boot faster.
This gives you an ncurses interface where you can
choose the desktop environment/window manager and the
driver.

The ATI driver in the LiveCD doesn't work with the ATI
7500 on T41. Well, its old and I don't think it will
support 3d and graphics acceleration. There is another
option for an nvidia driver. I chose the kernel driver
(last one) and it booted fine. But, the mouse movement
was pathetically slow due to:

(EE) RADEON (0): [agp] AGP failed to initialize.
Disabling DRI.

I think a desktop with a recent 3d, graphics
acceleration card (like nvidia) should suit this
distro.

And yes, you can also install lg3d-core to hard disk:

https://lg3d-core.dev.java.net/

https://lg3d-core.dev.java.net/lg3d-getting-started.html

I'll get a copy of the Live CD during our next meet.

Regards,

SK

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Thu Oct 27 17:40:21 2005
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (Ramkumar R)
Date: Thu Oct 27 17:40:29 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] accessing fat32 partition as non-root user
In-Reply-To: <5ef2113c0510270326h7bb335cbm82743f811ae1eb7c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <20051026163013.49334.qmail@web8410.mail.in.yahoo.com>
	<20051027100226.92537.qmail@web8502.mail.in.yahoo.com>
	<5ef2113c0510270326h7bb335cbm82743f811ae1eb7c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170510270510r5ad3ebe8hc6cde79addc411c3@mail.gmail.com>

> > /dev/hda1      /winc   vfat   rw,user,auto    0     0
>
> Try this
>
> /dev/hda1     /winc   vfat rw,user,noauto    0   0

i dont think that will solve the problem. vfat does not support
setting per file permissions. but u can tell the kernel what common
permissions are needed for files/dirs. check the dmask and fmask
options for fat in man mount. i think appending dmask=022,fmask=133
should do the trick... (dmask sets the same permission on all dirs,
fmask on all files)

it moves on...

On Thu, 2005-10-27 at 11:02 +0100, Ananth wrote:
> Hi,

> after a few years, i decided to reinstall debain from last year's pc quest

> permitted error.

FN's Eye on FLOSS (Free/Libre and Open Source Software) ........
